   39 import static java.lang.constant.ConstantDescs.BSM_EXPLICIT_CAST;
   40 import static java.lang.constant.ConstantDescs.CD_char;
   41 import static java.lang.constant.ConstantDescs.CD_int;
   42 import static java.lang.constant.ConstantDescs.DEFAULT_NAME;

   44 /**
   45  * The {@code Character} class wraps a value of the primitive
   46  * type {@code char} in an object. An object of class
   47  * {@code Character} contains a single field whose type is
   48  * {@code char}.
   49  * <p>
   50  * In addition, this class provides a large number of static methods for
   51  * determining a character's category (lowercase letter, digit, etc.)
   52  * and for converting characters from uppercase to lowercase and vice
   53  * versa.
   54  *
   55  * <h2><a id="conformance">Unicode Conformance</a></h2>
   56  * <p>
   57  * The fields and methods of class {@code Character} are defined in terms
   58  * of character information from the Unicode Standard, specifically the
   59  * <i>UnicodeData</i> file that is part of the Unicode Character Database.
   60  * This file specifies properties including name and category for every
   61  * assigned Unicode code point or character range. The file is available
   62  * from the Unicode Consortium at
   63  * <a href="http://www.unicode.org">http://www.unicode.org</a>.
   64  * <p>
   65  * Character information is based on the Unicode Standard, version 12.1.
   66  *
   67  * <h2><a id="unicode">Unicode Character Representations</a></h2>
   68  *
   69  * <p>The {@code char} data type (and therefore the value that a
   70  * {@code Character} object encapsulates) are based on the
   71  * original Unicode specification, which defined characters as
   72  * fixed-width 16-bit entities. The Unicode Standard has since been
   73  * changed to allow for characters whose representation requires more
   74  * than 16 bits.  The range of legal <em>code point</em>s is now
   75  * U+0000 to U+10FFFF, known as <em>Unicode scalar value</em>.
   76  * (Refer to the <a
   77  * href="http://www.unicode.org/reports/tr27/#notation"><i>
   78  * definition</i></a> of the U+<i>n</i> notation in the Unicode
   79  * Standard.)
   80  *
   81  * <p><a id="BMP">The set of characters from U+0000 to U+FFFF</a> is
   82  * sometimes referred to as the <em>Basic Multilingual Plane (BMP)</em>.
   83  * <a id="supplementary">Characters</a> whose code points are greater
   84  * than U+FFFF are called <em>supplementary character</em>s.  The Java
   85  * platform uses the UTF-16 representation in {@code char} arrays and
   86  * in the {@code String} and {@code StringBuffer} classes. In
   87  * this representation, supplementary characters are represented as a pair
   88  * of {@code char} values, the first from the <em>high-surrogates</em>
   89  * range, (&#92;uD800-&#92;uDBFF), the second from the
   90  * <em>low-surrogates</em> range (&#92;uDC00-&#92;uDFFF).
   91  *
   92  * <p>A {@code char} value, therefore, represents Basic
   93  * Multilingual Plane (BMP) code points, including the surrogate
   94  * code points, or code units of the UTF-16 encoding. An
   95  * {@code int} value represents all Unicode code points,
   96  * including supplementary code points. The lower (least significant)
   97  * 21 bits of {@code int} are used to represent Unicode code
   98  * points and the upper (most significant) 11 bits must be zero.
   99  * Unless otherwise specified, the behavior with respect to
  100  * supplementary characters and surrogate {@code char} values is
  101  * as follows:
  102  *
  103  * <ul>
  104  * <li>The methods that only accept a {@code char} value cannot support
  105  * supplementary characters. They treat {@code char} values from the
  106  * surrogate ranges as undefined characters. For example,
  107  * {@code Character.isLetter('\u005CuD840')} returns {@code false}, even though
  108  * this specific value if followed by any low-surrogate value in a string
  109  * would represent a letter.
  110  *
  111  * <li>The methods that accept an {@code int} value support all
  112  * Unicode characters, including supplementary characters. For
  113  * example, {@code Character.isLetter(0x2F81A)} returns
  114  * {@code true} because the code point value represents a letter
  115  * (a CJK ideograph).
  116  * </ul>
  117  *
  118  * <p>In the Java SE API documentation, <em>Unicode code point</em> is
  119  * used for character values in the range between U+0000 and U+10FFFF,
  120  * and <em>Unicode code unit</em> is used for 16-bit
  121  * {@code char} values that are code units of the <em>UTF-16</em>
  122  * encoding. For more information on Unicode terminology, refer to the
  123  * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/">Unicode Glossary</a>.
  124  *
  125  * @author  Lee Boynton
  126  * @author  Guy Steele
  127  * @author  Akira Tanaka
  128  * @author  Martin Buchholz
  129  * @author  Ulf Zibis
  130  * @since   1.0
  131  */
  132 public final
  133 class Character implements java.io.Serializable, Comparable<Character>, Constable {
  134     /**
  135      * The minimum radix available for conversion to and from strings.
  136      * The constant value of this field is the smallest value permitted
  137      * for the radix argument in radix-conversion methods such as the
  138      * {@code digit} method, the {@code forDigit} method, and the
  139      * {@code toString} method of class {@code Integer}.
  140      *
  141      * @see     Character#digit(char, int)
  142      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
  143      * @see     Integer#toString(int, int)
  144      * @see     Integer#valueOf(String)
  145      */
  146     public static final int MIN_RADIX = 2;
  147 
  148     /**
  149      * The maximum radix available for conversion to and from strings.
  150      * The constant value of this field is the largest value permitted
  151      * for the radix argument in radix-conversion methods such as the
  152      * {@code digit} method, the {@code forDigit} method, and the
  153      * {@code toString} method of class {@code Integer}.
  154      *
  155      * @see     Character#digit(char, int)
  156      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
  157      * @see     Integer#toString(int, int)
  158      * @see     Integer#valueOf(String)
  159      */
  160     public static final int MAX_RADIX = 36;
  161 
  162     /**
  163      * The constant value of this field is the smallest value of type
  164      * {@code char}, {@code '\u005Cu0000'}.
  165      *
  166      * @since   1.0.2
  167      */
  168     public static final char MIN_VALUE = '\u0000';
  169 
  170     /**
  171      * The constant value of this field is the largest value of type
  172      * {@code char}, {@code '\u005CuFFFF'}.
  173      *
  174      * @since   1.0.2
  175      */
  176     public static final char MAX_VALUE = '\uFFFF';

  612 
  613     /**
  614      * Returns an {@link Optional} containing the nominal descriptor for this
  615      * instance.
  616      *
  617      * @return an {@link Optional} describing the {@linkplain Character} instance
  618      * @since 15
  619      */
  620     @Override
  621     public Optional<DynamicConstantDesc<Character>> describeConstable() {
  622         return Optional.of(DynamicConstantDesc.ofNamed(BSM_EXPLICIT_CAST, DEFAULT_NAME, CD_char, (int) value));
  623     }
  624 
  625     /**
  626      * Instances of this class represent particular subsets of the Unicode
  627      * character set.  The only family of subsets defined in the
  628      * {@code Character} class is {@link Character.UnicodeBlock}.
  629      * Other portions of the Java API may define other subsets for their
  630      * own purposes.
  631      *
  632      * @since 1.2
  633      */
  634     public static class Subset  {
  635 
  636         private String name;
  637 
  638         /**
  639          * Constructs a new {@code Subset} instance.
  640          *
  641          * @param  name  The name of this subset
  642          * @throws NullPointerException if name is {@code null}
  643          */
  644         protected Subset(String name) {
  645             if (name == null) {
  646                 throw new NullPointerException("name");
  647             }
  648             this.name = name;
  649         }
  650 
  651         /**
  652          * Compares two {@code Subset} objects for equality.
  653          * This method returns {@code true} if and only if
  654          * {@code this} and the argument refer to the same
  655          * object; since this method is {@code final}, this
  656          * guarantee holds for all subclasses.
  657          */
  658         public final boolean equals(Object obj) {
  659             return (this == obj);
  660         }
  661 
  662         /**
  663          * Returns the standard hash code as defined by the
  664          * {@link Object#hashCode} method.  This method
  665          * is {@code final} in order to ensure that the
  666          * {@code equals} and {@code hashCode} methods will
  667          * be consistent in all subclasses.
  668          */
  669         public final int hashCode() {
  670             return super.hashCode();
  671         }
  672 
  673         /**
  674          * Returns the name of this subset.
  675          */
  676         public final String toString() {
  677             return name;
  678         }
  679     }
  680 
  681     // See http://www.unicode.org/Public/UNIDATA/Blocks.txt
  682     // for the latest specification of Unicode Blocks.
  683 
  684     /**
  685      * A family of character subsets representing the character blocks in the
  686      * Unicode specification. Character blocks generally define characters
  687      * used for a specific script or purpose. A character is contained by
  688      * at most one Unicode block.
  689      *
  690      * @since 1.2
  691      */
  692     public static final class UnicodeBlock extends Subset {
  693         /**
  694          * 676 - the expected number of entities
  695          * 0.75 - the default load factor of HashMap
  696          */
  697         private static final int NUM_ENTITIES = 676;
  698         private static Map<String, UnicodeBlock> map =
  699                 new HashMap<>((int)(NUM_ENTITIES / 0.75f + 1.0f));
  700 
  701         /**
  702          * Creates a UnicodeBlock with the given identifier name.
  703          * This name must be the same as the block identifier.
  704          */
  705         private UnicodeBlock(String idName) {
  706             super(idName);
  707             map.put(idName, this);
  708         }
  709 
  710         /**
  711          * Creates a UnicodeBlock with the given identifier name and
  712          * alias name.
  713          */
  714         private UnicodeBlock(String idName, String alias) {
  715             this(idName);
  716             map.put(alias, this);
  717         }
  718 
  719         /**
  720          * Creates a UnicodeBlock with the given identifier name and
  721          * alias names.
  722          */
  723         private UnicodeBlock(String idName, String... aliases) {
  724             this(idName);
  725             for (String alias : aliases)
  726                 map.put(alias, this);
  727         }
  728

 3307         private static final int[] blockStarts = {
 3308             0x0000,   // 0000..007F; Basic Latin
 3309             0x0080,   // 0080..00FF; Latin-1 Supplement
 3310             0x0100,   // 0100..017F; Latin Extended-A

 4020         /**
 4021          * Returns the object representing the Unicode block containing the
 4022          * given character, or {@code null} if the character is not a
 4023          * member of a defined block.
 4024          *
 4025          * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle
 4026          * <a href="Character.html#supplementary"> supplementary
 4027          * characters</a>.  To support all Unicode characters, including
 4028          * supplementary characters, use the {@link #of(int)} method.
 4029          *
 4030          * @param   c  The character in question
 4031          * @return  The {@code UnicodeBlock} instance representing the
 4032          *          Unicode block of which this character is a member, or
 4033          *          {@code null} if the character is not a member of any
 4034          *          Unicode block
 4035          */
 4036         public static UnicodeBlock of(char c) {
 4037             return of((int)c);
 4038         }
 4039 
 4040         /**
 4041          * Returns the object representing the Unicode block
 4042          * containing the given character (Unicode code point), or
 4043          * {@code null} if the character is not a member of a
 4044          * defined block.
 4045          *
 4046          * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) in question.
 4047          * @return  The {@code UnicodeBlock} instance representing the
 4048          *          Unicode block of which this character is a member, or
 4049          *          {@code null} if the character is not a member of any
 4050          *          Unicode block
 4051          * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 4052          * {@code codePoint} is an invalid Unicode code point.
 4053          * @see Character#isValidCodePoint(int)
 4054          * @since   1.5
 4055          */
 4056         public static UnicodeBlock of(int codePoint) {
 4057             if (!isValidCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 4058                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(
 4059                     String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
 4060             }
 4061 
 4062             int top, bottom, current;
 4063             bottom = 0;
 4064             top = blockStarts.length;
 4065             current = top/2;
 4066 
 4067             // invariant: top > current >= bottom && codePoint >= unicodeBlockStarts[bottom]
 4068             while (top - bottom > 1) {
 4069                 if (codePoint >= blockStarts[current]) {
 4070                     bottom = current;
 4071                 } else {
 4072                     top = current;
 4073                 }
 4074                 current = (top + bottom) / 2;
 4075             }
 4076             return blocks[current];
 4077         }
 4078 
 4079         /**
 4080          * Returns the UnicodeBlock with the given name. Block
 4081          * names are determined by The Unicode Standard. The file
 4082          * {@code Blocks-<version>.txt} defines blocks for a particular
 4083          * version of the standard. The {@link Character} class specifies
 4084          * the version of the standard that it supports.
 4085          * <p>
 4086          * This method accepts block names in the following forms:
 4087          * <ol>
 4088          * <li> Canonical block names as defined by the Unicode Standard.
 4089          * For example, the standard defines a "Basic Latin" block. Therefore, this
 4090          * method accepts "Basic Latin" as a valid block name. The documentation of
 4091          * each UnicodeBlock provides the canonical name.
 4092          * <li>Canonical block names with all spaces removed. For example, "BasicLatin"
 4093          * is a valid block name for the "Basic Latin" block.
 4094          * <li>The text representation of each constant UnicodeBlock identifier.
 4095          * For example, this method will return the {@link #BASIC_LATIN} block if
 4096          * provided with the "BASIC_LATIN" name. This form replaces all spaces and
 4097          * hyphens in the canonical name with underscores.
 4098          * </ol>
 4099          * Finally, character case is ignored for all of the valid block name forms.
 4100          * For example, "BASIC_LATIN" and "basic_latin" are both valid block names.
 4101          * The en_US locale's case mapping rules are used to provide case-insensitive
 4102          * string comparisons for block name validation.
 4103          * <p>
 4104          * If the Unicode Standard changes block names, both the previous and
 4105          * current names will be accepted.
 4106          *
 4107          * @param blockName A {@code UnicodeBlock} name.
 4108          * @return The {@code UnicodeBlock} instance identified
 4109          *         by {@code blockName}
 4110          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code blockName} is an
 4111          *         invalid name
 4112          * @throws NullPointerException if {@code blockName} is null
 4113          * @since 1.5
 4114          */
 4115         public static final UnicodeBlock forName(String blockName) {
 4116             UnicodeBlock block = map.get(blockName.toUpperCase(Locale.US));
 4117             if (block == null) {
 4118                 throw new IllegalArgumentException("Not a valid block name: "
 4119                             + blockName);
 4120             }
 4121             return block;
 4122         }
 4123     }

 8250         /**
 8251          * Returns the enum constant representing the Unicode script of which
 8252          * the given character (Unicode code point) is assigned to.
 8253          *
 8254          * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) in question.
 8255          * @return  The {@code UnicodeScript} constant representing the
 8256          *          Unicode script of which this character is assigned to.
 8257          *
 8258          * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 8259          * {@code codePoint} is an invalid Unicode code point.
 8260          * @see Character#isValidCodePoint(int)
 8261          *
 8262          */
 8263         public static UnicodeScript of(int codePoint) {
 8264             if (!isValidCodePoint(codePoint))
 8265                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(
 8266                     String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
 8267             int type = getType(codePoint);
 8268             // leave SURROGATE and PRIVATE_USE for table lookup
 8269             if (type == UNASSIGNED)
 8270                 return UNKNOWN;
 8271             int index = Arrays.binarySearch(scriptStarts, codePoint);
 8272             if (index < 0)
 8273                 index = -index - 2;
 8274             return scripts[index];
 8275         }
 8276 
 8277         /**
 8278          * Returns the UnicodeScript constant with the given Unicode script
 8279          * name or the script name alias. Script names and their aliases are
 8280          * determined by The Unicode Standard. The files {@code Scripts<version>.txt}
 8281          * and {@code PropertyValueAliases<version>.txt} define script names
 8282          * and the script name aliases for a particular version of the
 8283          * standard. The {@link Character} class specifies the version of
 8284          * the standard that it supports.
 8285          * <p>
 8286          * Character case is ignored for all of the valid script names.
 8287          * The en_US locale's case mapping rules are used to provide
 8288          * case-insensitive string comparisons for script name validation.
 8289          *
 8290          * @param scriptName A {@code UnicodeScript} name.
 8291          * @return The {@code UnicodeScript} constant identified
 8292          *         by {@code scriptName}
 8293          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code scriptName} is an
 8294          *         invalid name
 8295          * @throws NullPointerException if {@code scriptName} is null
 8296          */
 8297         public static final UnicodeScript forName(String scriptName) {
 8298             scriptName = scriptName.toUpperCase(Locale.ENGLISH);
 8299                                  //.replace(' ', '_'));
 8300             UnicodeScript sc = aliases.get(scriptName);
 8301             if (sc != null)
 8302                 return sc;
 8303             return valueOf(scriptName);
 8304         }
 8305     }
 8306 
 8307     /**
 8308      * The value of the {@code Character}.
 8309      *
 8310      * @serial
 8311      */
 8312     private final char value;
 8313 
 8314     /** use serialVersionUID from JDK 1.0.2 for interoperability */
 8315     @java.io.Serial
 8316     private static final long serialVersionUID = 3786198910865385080L;
 8317 
 8318     /**
 8319      * Constructs a newly allocated {@code Character} object that
 8320      * represents the specified {@code char} value.
 8321      *
 8322      * @param  value   the value to be represented by the
 8323      *                  {@code Character} object.
 8324      *
 8325      * @deprecated
 8326      * It is rarely appropriate to use this constructor. The static factory
 8327      * {@link #valueOf(char)} is generally a better choice, as it is
 8328      * likely to yield significantly better space and time performance.
 8329      */
 8330     @Deprecated(since="9")
 8331     public Character(char value) {
 8332         this.value = value;
 8333     }
 8334 
 8335     private static class CharacterCache {
 8336         private CharacterCache(){}
 8337 
 8338         static final Character[] cache;
 8339         static Character[] archivedCache;
 8340 
 8341         static {
 8342             int size = 127 + 1;
 8343 
 8344             // Load and use the archived cache if it exists
 8345             VM.initializeFromArchive(CharacterCache.class);
 8346             if (archivedCache == null || archivedCache.length != size) {
 8347                 Character[] c = new Character[size];
 8348                 for (int i = 0; i < size; i++) {
 8349                     c[i] = new Character((char) i);
 8350                 }
 8351                 archivedCache = c;
 8352             }
 8353             cache = archivedCache;
 8354         }
 8355     }
 8356 
 8357     /**
 8358      * Returns a {@code Character} instance representing the specified
 8359      * {@code char} value.
 8360      * If a new {@code Character} instance is not required, this method
 8361      * should generally be used in preference to the constructor
 8362      * {@link #Character(char)}, as this method is likely to yield
 8363      * significantly better space and time performance by caching
 8364      * frequently requested values.
 8365      *
 8366      * This method will always cache values in the range {@code
 8367      * '\u005Cu0000'} to {@code '\u005Cu007F'}, inclusive, and may
 8368      * cache other values outside of this range.
 8369      *
 8370      * @param  c a char value.
 8371      * @return a {@code Character} instance representing {@code c}.
 8372      * @since  1.5
 8373      */
 8374     @HotSpotIntrinsicCandidate
 8375     public static Character valueOf(char c) {
 8376         if (c <= 127) { // must cache
 8377             return CharacterCache.cache[(int)c];
 8378         }
 8379         return new Character(c);
 8380     }
 8381 
 8382     /**
 8383      * Returns the value of this {@code Character} object.
 8384      * @return  the primitive {@code char} value represented by
 8385      *          this object.
 8386      */
 8387     @HotSpotIntrinsicCandidate
 8388     public char charValue() {
 8389         return value;
 8390     }

 8392     /**
 8393      * Returns a hash code for this {@code Character}; equal to the result
 8394      * of invoking {@code charValue()}.
 8395      *
 8396      * @return a hash code value for this {@code Character}
 8397      */
 8398     @Override
 8399     public int hashCode() {
 8400         return Character.hashCode(value);
 8401     }

 8403     /**
 8404      * Returns a hash code for a {@code char} value; compatible with
 8405      * {@code Character.hashCode()}.
 8406      *
 8407      * @since 1.8
 8408      *
 8409      * @param value The {@code char} for which to return a hash code.
 8410      * @return a hash code value for a {@code char} value.
 8411      */
 8412     public static int hashCode(char value) {
 8413         return (int)value;
 8414     }

 8416     /**
 8417      * Compares this object against the specified object.
 8418      * The result is {@code true} if and only if the argument is not
 8419      * {@code null} and is a {@code Character} object that
 8420      * represents the same {@code char} value as this object.
 8421      *
 8422      * @param   obj   the object to compare with.
 8423      * @return  {@code true} if the objects are the same;
 8424      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 8425      */
 8426     public boolean equals(Object obj) {
 8427         if (obj instanceof Character) {
 8428             return value == ((Character)obj).charValue();
 8429         }
 8430         return false;
 8431     }

 8433     /**
 8434      * Returns a {@code String} object representing this
 8435      * {@code Character}'s value.  The result is a string of
 8436      * length 1 whose sole component is the primitive
 8437      * {@code char} value represented by this
 8438      * {@code Character} object.
 8439      *
 8440      * @return  a string representation of this object.
 8441      */
 8442     public String toString() {
 8443         return String.valueOf(value);
 8444     }

 8446     /**
 8447      * Returns a {@code String} object representing the
 8448      * specified {@code char}.  The result is a string of length
 8449      * 1 consisting solely of the specified {@code char}.
 8450      *
 8451      * @apiNote This method cannot handle <a
 8452      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 8453      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 8454      * the {@link #toString(int)} method.
 8455      *
 8456      * @param c the {@code char} to be converted
 8457      * @return the string representation of the specified {@code char}
 8458      * @since 1.4
 8459      */
 8460     public static String toString(char c) {
 8461         return String.valueOf(c);
 8462     }

 8464     /**
 8465      * Returns a {@code String} object representing the
 8466      * specified character (Unicode code point).  The result is a string of
 8467      * length 1 or 2, consisting solely of the specified {@code codePoint}.
 8468      *
 8469      * @param codePoint the {@code codePoint} to be converted
 8470      * @return the string representation of the specified {@code codePoint}
 8471      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 8472      *      {@code codePoint} is not a {@linkplain #isValidCodePoint
 8473      *      valid Unicode code point}.
 8474      * @since 11
 8475      */
 8476     public static String toString(int codePoint) {
 8477         return String.valueOfCodePoint(codePoint);
 8478     }
 8479 
 8480     /**
 8481      * Determines whether the specified code point is a valid
 8482      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#code_point">
 8483      * Unicode code point value</a>.
 8484      *
 8485      * @param  codePoint the Unicode code point to be tested
 8486      * @return {@code true} if the specified code point value is between
 8487      *         {@link #MIN_CODE_POINT} and
 8488      *         {@link #MAX_CODE_POINT} inclusive;
 8489      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8490      * @since  1.5
 8491      */
 8492     public static boolean isValidCodePoint(int codePoint) {
 8493         // Optimized form of:
 8494         //     codePoint >= MIN_CODE_POINT && codePoint <= MAX_CODE_POINT
 8495         int plane = codePoint >>> 16;
 8496         return plane < ((MAX_CODE_POINT + 1) >>> 16);
 8497     }
 8498 
 8499     /**
 8500      * Determines whether the specified character (Unicode code point)
 8501      * is in the <a href="#BMP">Basic Multilingual Plane (BMP)</a>.
 8502      * Such code points can be represented using a single {@code char}.
 8503      *
 8504      * @param  codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested
 8505      * @return {@code true} if the specified code point is between
 8506      *         {@link #MIN_VALUE} and {@link #MAX_VALUE} inclusive;
 8507      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8508      * @since  1.7
 8509      */
 8510     public static boolean isBmpCodePoint(int codePoint) {
 8511         return codePoint >>> 16 == 0;
 8512         // Optimized form of:
 8513         //     codePoint >= MIN_VALUE && codePoint <= MAX_VALUE
 8514         // We consistently use logical shift (>>>) to facilitate
 8515         // additional runtime optimizations.
 8516     }
 8517 
 8518     /**
 8519      * Determines whether the specified character (Unicode code point)
 8520      * is in the <a href="#supplementary">supplementary character</a> range.
 8521      *
 8522      * @param  codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested
 8523      * @return {@code true} if the specified code point is between
 8524      *         {@link #MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT} and
 8525      *         {@link #MAX_CODE_POINT} inclusive;
 8526      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8527      * @since  1.5
 8528      */
 8529     public static boolean isSupplementaryCodePoint(int codePoint) {
 8530         return codePoint >= MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT
 8531             && codePoint <  MAX_CODE_POINT + 1;
 8532     }
 8533 
 8534     /**
 8535      * Determines if the given {@code char} value is a
 8536      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#high_surrogate_code_unit">
 8537      * Unicode high-surrogate code unit</a>
 8538      * (also known as <i>leading-surrogate code unit</i>).
 8539      *
 8540      * <p>Such values do not represent characters by themselves,
 8541      * but are used in the representation of
 8542      * <a href="#supplementary">supplementary characters</a>
 8543      * in the UTF-16 encoding.
 8544      *
 8545      * @param  ch the {@code char} value to be tested.
 8546      * @return {@code true} if the {@code char} value is between
 8547      *         {@link #MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE} and
 8548      *         {@link #MAX_HIGH_SURROGATE} inclusive;
 8549      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8550      * @see    Character#isLowSurrogate(char)
 8551      * @see    Character.UnicodeBlock#of(int)
 8552      * @since  1.5
 8553      */
 8554     public static boolean isHighSurrogate(char ch) {
 8555         // Help VM constant-fold; MAX_HIGH_SURROGATE + 1 == MIN_LOW_SURROGATE
 8556         return ch >= MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE && ch < (MAX_HIGH_SURROGATE + 1);
 8557     }
 8558 
 8559     /**
 8560      * Determines if the given {@code char} value is a
 8561      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#low_surrogate_code_unit">
 8562      * Unicode low-surrogate code unit</a>
 8563      * (also known as <i>trailing-surrogate code unit</i>).
 8564      *
 8565      * <p>Such values do not represent characters by themselves,
 8566      * but are used in the representation of
 8567      * <a href="#supplementary">supplementary characters</a>
 8568      * in the UTF-16 encoding.
 8569      *
 8570      * @param  ch the {@code char} value to be tested.
 8571      * @return {@code true} if the {@code char} value is between
 8572      *         {@link #MIN_LOW_SURROGATE} and
 8573      *         {@link #MAX_LOW_SURROGATE} inclusive;
 8574      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8575      * @see    Character#isHighSurrogate(char)
 8576      * @since  1.5
 8577      */
 8578     public static boolean isLowSurrogate(char ch) {
 8579         return ch >= MIN_LOW_SURROGATE && ch < (MAX_LOW_SURROGATE + 1);
 8580     }
 8581 
 8582     /**
 8583      * Determines if the given {@code char} value is a Unicode
 8584      * <i>surrogate code unit</i>.
 8585      *
 8586      * <p>Such values do not represent characters by themselves,
 8587      * but are used in the representation of
 8588      * <a href="#supplementary">supplementary characters</a>
 8589      * in the UTF-16 encoding.
 8590      *
 8591      * <p>A char value is a surrogate code unit if and only if it is either
 8592      * a {@linkplain #isLowSurrogate(char) low-surrogate code unit} or
 8593      * a {@linkplain #isHighSurrogate(char) high-surrogate code unit}.
 8594      *
 8595      * @param  ch the {@code char} value to be tested.
 8596      * @return {@code true} if the {@code char} value is between
 8597      *         {@link #MIN_SURROGATE} and
 8598      *         {@link #MAX_SURROGATE} inclusive;
 8599      *         {@code false} otherwise.
 8600      * @since  1.7
 8601      */
 8602     public static boolean isSurrogate(char ch) {
 8603         return ch >= MIN_SURROGATE && ch < (MAX_SURROGATE + 1);
 8604     }
 8605 
 8606     /**
 8607      * Determines whether the specified pair of {@code char}
 8608      * values is a valid
 8609      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_pair">
 8610      * Unicode surrogate pair</a>.
 8611      *
 8612      * <p>This method is equivalent to the expression:
 8613      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
 8614      * isHighSurrogate(high) && isLowSurrogate(low)
 8615      * }</pre></blockquote>
 8616      *
 8617      * @param  high the high-surrogate code value to be tested
 8618      * @param  low the low-surrogate code value to be tested
 8619      * @return {@code true} if the specified high and
 8620      * low-surrogate code values represent a valid surrogate pair;
 8621      * {@code false} otherwise.
 8622      * @since  1.5
 8623      */
 8624     public static boolean isSurrogatePair(char high, char low) {
 8625         return isHighSurrogate(high) && isLowSurrogate(low);
 8626     }
 8627 
 8628     /**
 8629      * Determines the number of {@code char} values needed to
 8630      * represent the specified character (Unicode code point). If the
 8631      * specified character is equal to or greater than 0x10000, then
 8632      * the method returns 2. Otherwise, the method returns 1.
 8633      *
 8634      * <p>This method doesn't validate the specified character to be a
 8635      * valid Unicode code point. The caller must validate the
 8636      * character value using {@link #isValidCodePoint(int) isValidCodePoint}
 8637      * if necessary.
 8638      *
 8639      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 8640      * @return  2 if the character is a valid supplementary character; 1 otherwise.
 8641      * @see     Character#isSupplementaryCodePoint(int)
 8642      * @since   1.5
 8643      */
 8644     public static int charCount(int codePoint) {
 8645         return codePoint >= MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT ? 2 : 1;
 8646     }
 8647 
 8648     /**
 8649      * Converts the specified surrogate pair to its supplementary code
 8650      * point value. This method does not validate the specified
 8651      * surrogate pair. The caller must validate it using {@link
 8652      * #isSurrogatePair(char, char) isSurrogatePair} if necessary.
 8653      *
 8654      * @param  high the high-surrogate code unit
 8655      * @param  low the low-surrogate code unit
 8656      * @return the supplementary code point composed from the
 8657      *         specified surrogate pair.
 8658      * @since  1.5
 8659      */
 8660     public static int toCodePoint(char high, char low) {
 8661         // Optimized form of:
 8662         // return ((high - MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE) << 10)
 8663         //         + (low - MIN_LOW_SURROGATE)
 8664         //         + MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT;
 8665         return ((high << 10) + low) + (MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT
 8666                                        - (MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE << 10)
 8667                                        - MIN_LOW_SURROGATE);
 8668     }
 8669 
 8670     /**
 8671      * Returns the code point at the given index of the
 8672      * {@code CharSequence}. If the {@code char} value at
 8673      * the given index in the {@code CharSequence} is in the
 8674      * high-surrogate range, the following index is less than the
 8675      * length of the {@code CharSequence}, and the
 8676      * {@code char} value at the following index is in the
 8677      * low-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8678      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8679      * the {@code char} value at the given index is returned.
 8680      *
 8681      * @param seq a sequence of {@code char} values (Unicode code
 8682      * units)
 8683      * @param index the index to the {@code char} values (Unicode
 8684      * code units) in {@code seq} to be converted
 8685      * @return the Unicode code point at the given index
 8686      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code seq} is null.
 8687      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the value
 8688      * {@code index} is negative or not less than
 8689      * {@link CharSequence#length() seq.length()}.
 8690      * @since  1.5
 8691      */
 8692     public static int codePointAt(CharSequence seq, int index) {
 8693         char c1 = seq.charAt(index);
 8694         if (isHighSurrogate(c1) && ++index < seq.length()) {
 8695             char c2 = seq.charAt(index);
 8696             if (isLowSurrogate(c2)) {
 8697                 return toCodePoint(c1, c2);
 8698             }
 8699         }
 8700         return c1;
 8701     }
 8702 
 8703     /**
 8704      * Returns the code point at the given index of the
 8705      * {@code char} array. If the {@code char} value at
 8706      * the given index in the {@code char} array is in the
 8707      * high-surrogate range, the following index is less than the
 8708      * length of the {@code char} array, and the
 8709      * {@code char} value at the following index is in the
 8710      * low-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8711      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8712      * the {@code char} value at the given index is returned.
 8713      *
 8714      * @param a the {@code char} array
 8715      * @param index the index to the {@code char} values (Unicode
 8716      * code units) in the {@code char} array to be converted
 8717      * @return the Unicode code point at the given index
 8718      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 8719      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the value
 8720      * {@code index} is negative or not less than
 8721      * the length of the {@code char} array.
 8722      * @since  1.5
 8723      */
 8724     public static int codePointAt(char[] a, int index) {
 8725         return codePointAtImpl(a, index, a.length);
 8726     }
 8727 
 8728     /**
 8729      * Returns the code point at the given index of the
 8730      * {@code char} array, where only array elements with
 8731      * {@code index} less than {@code limit} can be used. If
 8732      * the {@code char} value at the given index in the
 8733      * {@code char} array is in the high-surrogate range, the
 8734      * following index is less than the {@code limit}, and the
 8735      * {@code char} value at the following index is in the
 8736      * low-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8737      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8738      * the {@code char} value at the given index is returned.
 8739      *
 8740      * @param a the {@code char} array
 8741      * @param index the index to the {@code char} values (Unicode
 8742      * code units) in the {@code char} array to be converted
 8743      * @param limit the index after the last array element that
 8744      * can be used in the {@code char} array
 8745      * @return the Unicode code point at the given index
 8746      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 8747      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the {@code index}
 8748      * argument is negative or not less than the {@code limit}
 8749      * argument, or if the {@code limit} argument is negative or
 8750      * greater than the length of the {@code char} array.
 8751      * @since  1.5
 8752      */
 8753     public static int codePointAt(char[] a, int index, int limit) {
 8754         if (index >= limit || limit < 0 || limit > a.length) {
 8755             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 8756         }
 8757         return codePointAtImpl(a, index, limit);
 8758     }
 8759 
 8760     // throws ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException if index out of bounds
 8761     static int codePointAtImpl(char[] a, int index, int limit) {
 8762         char c1 = a[index];
 8763         if (isHighSurrogate(c1) && ++index < limit) {
 8764             char c2 = a[index];
 8765             if (isLowSurrogate(c2)) {
 8766                 return toCodePoint(c1, c2);
 8767             }
 8768         }
 8769         return c1;
 8770     }
 8771 
 8772     /**
 8773      * Returns the code point preceding the given index of the
 8774      * {@code CharSequence}. If the {@code char} value at
 8775      * {@code (index - 1)} in the {@code CharSequence} is in
 8776      * the low-surrogate range, {@code (index - 2)} is not
 8777      * negative, and the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 2)}
 8778      * in the {@code CharSequence} is in the
 8779      * high-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8780      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8781      * the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 1)} is
 8782      * returned.
 8783      *
 8784      * @param seq the {@code CharSequence} instance
 8785      * @param index the index following the code point that should be returned
 8786      * @return the Unicode code point value before the given index.
 8787      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code seq} is null.
 8788      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the {@code index}
 8789      * argument is less than 1 or greater than {@link
 8790      * CharSequence#length() seq.length()}.
 8791      * @since  1.5
 8792      */
 8793     public static int codePointBefore(CharSequence seq, int index) {
 8794         char c2 = seq.charAt(--index);
 8795         if (isLowSurrogate(c2) && index > 0) {
 8796             char c1 = seq.charAt(--index);
 8797             if (isHighSurrogate(c1)) {
 8798                 return toCodePoint(c1, c2);
 8799             }
 8800         }
 8801         return c2;
 8802     }
 8803 
 8804     /**
 8805      * Returns the code point preceding the given index of the
 8806      * {@code char} array. If the {@code char} value at
 8807      * {@code (index - 1)} in the {@code char} array is in
 8808      * the low-surrogate range, {@code (index - 2)} is not
 8809      * negative, and the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 2)}
 8810      * in the {@code char} array is in the
 8811      * high-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8812      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8813      * the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 1)} is
 8814      * returned.
 8815      *
 8816      * @param a the {@code char} array
 8817      * @param index the index following the code point that should be returned
 8818      * @return the Unicode code point value before the given index.
 8819      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 8820      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the {@code index}
 8821      * argument is less than 1 or greater than the length of the
 8822      * {@code char} array
 8823      * @since  1.5
 8824      */
 8825     public static int codePointBefore(char[] a, int index) {
 8826         return codePointBeforeImpl(a, index, 0);
 8827     }
 8828 
 8829     /**
 8830      * Returns the code point preceding the given index of the
 8831      * {@code char} array, where only array elements with
 8832      * {@code index} greater than or equal to {@code start}
 8833      * can be used. If the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 1)}
 8834      * in the {@code char} array is in the
 8835      * low-surrogate range, {@code (index - 2)} is not less than
 8836      * {@code start}, and the {@code char} value at
 8837      * {@code (index - 2)} in the {@code char} array is in
 8838      * the high-surrogate range, then the supplementary code point
 8839      * corresponding to this surrogate pair is returned. Otherwise,
 8840      * the {@code char} value at {@code (index - 1)} is
 8841      * returned.
 8842      *
 8843      * @param a the {@code char} array
 8844      * @param index the index following the code point that should be returned
 8845      * @param start the index of the first array element in the
 8846      * {@code char} array
 8847      * @return the Unicode code point value before the given index.
 8848      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 8849      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the {@code index}
 8850      * argument is not greater than the {@code start} argument or
 8851      * is greater than the length of the {@code char} array, or
 8852      * if the {@code start} argument is negative or not less than
 8853      * the length of the {@code char} array.
 8854      * @since  1.5
 8855      */
 8856     public static int codePointBefore(char[] a, int index, int start) {
 8857         if (index <= start || start < 0 || start >= a.length) {
 8858             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 8859         }
 8860         return codePointBeforeImpl(a, index, start);
 8861     }
 8862 
 8863     // throws ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException if index-1 out of bounds
 8864     static int codePointBeforeImpl(char[] a, int index, int start) {
 8865         char c2 = a[--index];
 8866         if (isLowSurrogate(c2) && index > start) {
 8867             char c1 = a[--index];
 8868             if (isHighSurrogate(c1)) {
 8869                 return toCodePoint(c1, c2);
 8870             }
 8871         }
 8872         return c2;
 8873     }
 8874 
 8875     /**
 8876      * Returns the leading surrogate (a
 8877      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#high_surrogate_code_unit">
 8878      * high surrogate code unit</a>) of the
 8879      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_pair">
 8880      * surrogate pair</a>
 8881      * representing the specified supplementary character (Unicode
 8882      * code point) in the UTF-16 encoding.  If the specified character
 8883      * is not a
 8884      * <a href="Character.html#supplementary">supplementary character</a>,
 8885      * an unspecified {@code char} is returned.
 8886      *
 8887      * <p>If
 8888      * {@link #isSupplementaryCodePoint isSupplementaryCodePoint(x)}
 8889      * is {@code true}, then
 8890      * {@link #isHighSurrogate isHighSurrogate}{@code (highSurrogate(x))} and
 8891      * {@link #toCodePoint toCodePoint}{@code (highSurrogate(x), }{@link #lowSurrogate lowSurrogate}{@code (x)) == x}
 8892      * are also always {@code true}.
 8893      *
 8894      * @param   codePoint a supplementary character (Unicode code point)
 8895      * @return  the leading surrogate code unit used to represent the
 8896      *          character in the UTF-16 encoding
 8897      * @since   1.7
 8898      */
 8899     public static char highSurrogate(int codePoint) {
 8900         return (char) ((codePoint >>> 10)
 8901             + (MIN_HIGH_SURROGATE - (MIN_SUPPLEMENTARY_CODE_POINT >>> 10)));
 8902     }
 8903 
 8904     /**
 8905      * Returns the trailing surrogate (a
 8906      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#low_surrogate_code_unit">
 8907      * low surrogate code unit</a>) of the
 8908      * <a href="http://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_pair">
 8909      * surrogate pair</a>
 8910      * representing the specified supplementary character (Unicode
 8911      * code point) in the UTF-16 encoding.  If the specified character
 8912      * is not a
 8913      * <a href="Character.html#supplementary">supplementary character</a>,
 8914      * an unspecified {@code char} is returned.
 8915      *
 8916      * <p>If
 8917      * {@link #isSupplementaryCodePoint isSupplementaryCodePoint(x)}
 8918      * is {@code true}, then
 8919      * {@link #isLowSurrogate isLowSurrogate}{@code (lowSurrogate(x))} and
 8920      * {@link #toCodePoint toCodePoint}{@code (}{@link #highSurrogate highSurrogate}{@code (x), lowSurrogate(x)) == x}
 8921      * are also always {@code true}.
 8922      *
 8923      * @param   codePoint a supplementary character (Unicode code point)
 8924      * @return  the trailing surrogate code unit used to represent the
 8925      *          character in the UTF-16 encoding
 8926      * @since   1.7
 8927      */
 8928     public static char lowSurrogate(int codePoint) {
 8929         return (char) ((codePoint & 0x3ff) + MIN_LOW_SURROGATE);
 8930     }
 8931 
 8932     /**
 8933      * Converts the specified character (Unicode code point) to its
 8934      * UTF-16 representation. If the specified code point is a BMP
 8935      * (Basic Multilingual Plane or Plane 0) value, the same value is
 8936      * stored in {@code dst[dstIndex]}, and 1 is returned. If the
 8937      * specified code point is a supplementary character, its
 8938      * surrogate values are stored in {@code dst[dstIndex]}
 8939      * (high-surrogate) and {@code dst[dstIndex+1]}
 8940      * (low-surrogate), and 2 is returned.
 8941      *
 8942      * @param  codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be converted.
 8943      * @param  dst an array of {@code char} in which the
 8944      * {@code codePoint}'s UTF-16 value is stored.
 8945      * @param dstIndex the start index into the {@code dst}
 8946      * array where the converted value is stored.
 8947      * @return 1 if the code point is a BMP code point, 2 if the
 8948      * code point is a supplementary code point.
 8949      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 8950      * {@code codePoint} is not a valid Unicode code point.
 8951      * @throws NullPointerException if the specified {@code dst} is null.
 8952      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if {@code dstIndex}
 8953      * is negative or not less than {@code dst.length}, or if
 8954      * {@code dst} at {@code dstIndex} doesn't have enough
 8955      * array element(s) to store the resulting {@code char}
 8956      * value(s). (If {@code dstIndex} is equal to
 8957      * {@code dst.length-1} and the specified
 8958      * {@code codePoint} is a supplementary character, the
 8959      * high-surrogate value is not stored in
 8960      * {@code dst[dstIndex]}.)
 8961      * @since  1.5
 8962      */
 8963     public static int toChars(int codePoint, char[] dst, int dstIndex) {
 8964         if (isBmpCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 8965             dst[dstIndex] = (char) codePoint;
 8966             return 1;
 8967         } else if (isValidCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 8968             toSurrogates(codePoint, dst, dstIndex);
 8969             return 2;
 8970         } else {
 8971             throw new IllegalArgumentException(
 8972                 String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
 8973         }
 8974     }
 8975 
 8976     /**
 8977      * Converts the specified character (Unicode code point) to its
 8978      * UTF-16 representation stored in a {@code char} array. If
 8979      * the specified code point is a BMP (Basic Multilingual Plane or
 8980      * Plane 0) value, the resulting {@code char} array has
 8981      * the same value as {@code codePoint}. If the specified code
 8982      * point is a supplementary code point, the resulting
 8983      * {@code char} array has the corresponding surrogate pair.
 8984      *
 8985      * @param  codePoint a Unicode code point
 8986      * @return a {@code char} array having
 8987      *         {@code codePoint}'s UTF-16 representation.
 8988      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified
 8989      * {@code codePoint} is not a valid Unicode code point.
 8990      * @since  1.5
 8991      */
 8992     public static char[] toChars(int codePoint) {
 8993         if (isBmpCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 8994             return new char[] { (char) codePoint };
 8995         } else if (isValidCodePoint(codePoint)) {
 8996             char[] result = new char[2];
 8997             toSurrogates(codePoint, result, 0);
 8998             return result;
 8999         } else {
 9000             throw new IllegalArgumentException(
 9001                 String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
 9002         }
 9003     }
 9004 
 9005     static void toSurrogates(int codePoint, char[] dst, int index) {
 9006         // We write elements "backwards" to guarantee all-or-nothing
 9007         dst[index+1] = lowSurrogate(codePoint);
 9008         dst[index] = highSurrogate(codePoint);
 9009     }
 9010 
 9011     /**
 9012      * Returns the number of Unicode code points in the text range of
 9013      * the specified char sequence. The text range begins at the
 9014      * specified {@code beginIndex} and extends to the
 9015      * {@code char} at index {@code endIndex - 1}. Thus the
 9016      * length (in {@code char}s) of the text range is
 9017      * {@code endIndex-beginIndex}. Unpaired surrogates within
 9018      * the text range count as one code point each.
 9019      *
 9020      * @param seq the char sequence
 9021      * @param beginIndex the index to the first {@code char} of
 9022      * the text range.
 9023      * @param endIndex the index after the last {@code char} of
 9024      * the text range.
 9025      * @return the number of Unicode code points in the specified text
 9026      * range
 9027      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code seq} is null.
 9028      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if the
 9029      * {@code beginIndex} is negative, or {@code endIndex}
 9030      * is larger than the length of the given sequence, or
 9031      * {@code beginIndex} is larger than {@code endIndex}.
 9032      * @since  1.5
 9033      */
 9034     public static int codePointCount(CharSequence seq, int beginIndex, int endIndex) {
 9035         int length = seq.length();
 9036         if (beginIndex < 0 || endIndex > length || beginIndex > endIndex) {
 9037             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9038         }
 9039         int n = endIndex - beginIndex;
 9040         for (int i = beginIndex; i < endIndex; ) {
 9041             if (isHighSurrogate(seq.charAt(i++)) && i < endIndex &&
 9042                 isLowSurrogate(seq.charAt(i))) {
 9043                 n--;
 9044                 i++;
 9045             }
 9046         }
 9047         return n;
 9048     }
 9049 
 9050     /**
 9051      * Returns the number of Unicode code points in a subarray of the
 9052      * {@code char} array argument. The {@code offset}
 9053      * argument is the index of the first {@code char} of the
 9054      * subarray and the {@code count} argument specifies the
 9055      * length of the subarray in {@code char}s. Unpaired
 9056      * surrogates within the subarray count as one code point each.
 9057      *
 9058      * @param a the {@code char} array
 9059      * @param offset the index of the first {@code char} in the
 9060      * given {@code char} array
 9061      * @param count the length of the subarray in {@code char}s
 9062      * @return the number of Unicode code points in the specified subarray
 9063      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 9064      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if {@code offset} or
 9065      * {@code count} is negative, or if {@code offset +
 9066      * count} is larger than the length of the given array.
 9067      * @since  1.5
 9068      */
 9069     public static int codePointCount(char[] a, int offset, int count) {
 9070         if (count > a.length - offset || offset < 0 || count < 0) {
 9071             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9072         }
 9073         return codePointCountImpl(a, offset, count);
 9074     }
 9075 
 9076     static int codePointCountImpl(char[] a, int offset, int count) {
 9077         int endIndex = offset + count;
 9078         int n = count;
 9079         for (int i = offset; i < endIndex; ) {
 9080             if (isHighSurrogate(a[i++]) && i < endIndex &&
 9081                 isLowSurrogate(a[i])) {
 9082                 n--;
 9083                 i++;
 9084             }
 9085         }
 9086         return n;
 9087     }
 9088 
 9089     /**
 9090      * Returns the index within the given char sequence that is offset
 9091      * from the given {@code index} by {@code codePointOffset}
 9092      * code points. Unpaired surrogates within the text range given by
 9093      * {@code index} and {@code codePointOffset} count as
 9094      * one code point each.
 9095      *
 9096      * @param seq the char sequence
 9097      * @param index the index to be offset
 9098      * @param codePointOffset the offset in code points
 9099      * @return the index within the char sequence
 9100      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code seq} is null.
 9101      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException if {@code index}
 9102      *   is negative or larger then the length of the char sequence,
 9103      *   or if {@code codePointOffset} is positive and the
 9104      *   subsequence starting with {@code index} has fewer than
 9105      *   {@code codePointOffset} code points, or if
 9106      *   {@code codePointOffset} is negative and the subsequence
 9107      *   before {@code index} has fewer than the absolute value
 9108      *   of {@code codePointOffset} code points.
 9109      * @since 1.5
 9110      */
 9111     public static int offsetByCodePoints(CharSequence seq, int index,
 9112                                          int codePointOffset) {
 9113         int length = seq.length();
 9114         if (index < 0 || index > length) {
 9115             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9116         }
 9117 
 9118         int x = index;
 9119         if (codePointOffset >= 0) {
 9120             int i;
 9121             for (i = 0; x < length && i < codePointOffset; i++) {
 9122                 if (isHighSurrogate(seq.charAt(x++)) && x < length &&
 9123                     isLowSurrogate(seq.charAt(x))) {
 9124                     x++;
 9125                 }
 9126             }
 9127             if (i < codePointOffset) {
 9128                 throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9129             }
 9130         } else {
 9131             int i;
 9132             for (i = codePointOffset; x > 0 && i < 0; i++) {
 9133                 if (isLowSurrogate(seq.charAt(--x)) && x > 0 &&
 9134                     isHighSurrogate(seq.charAt(x-1))) {
 9135                     x--;
 9136                 }
 9137             }
 9138             if (i < 0) {
 9139                 throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9140             }
 9141         }
 9142         return x;
 9143     }
 9144 
 9145     /**
 9146      * Returns the index within the given {@code char} subarray
 9147      * that is offset from the given {@code index} by
 9148      * {@code codePointOffset} code points. The
 9149      * {@code start} and {@code count} arguments specify a
 9150      * subarray of the {@code char} array. Unpaired surrogates
 9151      * within the text range given by {@code index} and
 9152      * {@code codePointOffset} count as one code point each.
 9153      *
 9154      * @param a the {@code char} array
 9155      * @param start the index of the first {@code char} of the
 9156      * subarray
 9157      * @param count the length of the subarray in {@code char}s
 9158      * @param index the index to be offset
 9159      * @param codePointOffset the offset in code points
 9160      * @return the index within the subarray
 9161      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code a} is null.
 9162      * @throws IndexOutOfBoundsException
 9163      *   if {@code start} or {@code count} is negative,
 9164      *   or if {@code start + count} is larger than the length of
 9165      *   the given array,
 9166      *   or if {@code index} is less than {@code start} or
 9167      *   larger then {@code start + count},
 9168      *   or if {@code codePointOffset} is positive and the text range
 9169      *   starting with {@code index} and ending with {@code start + count - 1}
 9170      *   has fewer than {@code codePointOffset} code
 9171      *   points,
 9172      *   or if {@code codePointOffset} is negative and the text range
 9173      *   starting with {@code start} and ending with {@code index - 1}
 9174      *   has fewer than the absolute value of
 9175      *   {@code codePointOffset} code points.
 9176      * @since 1.5
 9177      */
 9178     public static int offsetByCodePoints(char[] a, int start, int count,
 9179                                          int index, int codePointOffset) {
 9180         if (count > a.length-start || start < 0 || count < 0
 9181             || index < start || index > start+count) {
 9182             throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9183         }
 9184         return offsetByCodePointsImpl(a, start, count, index, codePointOffset);
 9185     }
 9186 
 9187     static int offsetByCodePointsImpl(char[]a, int start, int count,
 9188                                       int index, int codePointOffset) {
 9189         int x = index;
 9190         if (codePointOffset >= 0) {
 9191             int limit = start + count;
 9192             int i;
 9193             for (i = 0; x < limit && i < codePointOffset; i++) {
 9194                 if (isHighSurrogate(a[x++]) && x < limit &&
 9195                     isLowSurrogate(a[x])) {
 9196                     x++;
 9197                 }
 9198             }
 9199             if (i < codePointOffset) {
 9200                 throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9201             }
 9202         } else {
 9203             int i;
 9204             for (i = codePointOffset; x > start && i < 0; i++) {
 9205                 if (isLowSurrogate(a[--x]) && x > start &&
 9206                     isHighSurrogate(a[x-1])) {
 9207                     x--;
 9208                 }
 9209             }
 9210             if (i < 0) {
 9211                 throw new IndexOutOfBoundsException();
 9212             }
 9213         }
 9214         return x;
 9215     }

 9217     /**
 9218      * Determines if the specified character is a lowercase character.
 9219      * <p>
 9220      * A character is lowercase if its general category type, provided
 9221      * by {@code Character.getType(ch)}, is
 9222      * {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}, or it has contributory property
 9223      * Other_Lowercase as defined by the Unicode Standard.
 9224      * <p>
 9225      * The following are examples of lowercase characters:
 9226      * <blockquote><pre>
 9227      * a b c d e f g h i j k l m n o p q r s t u v w x y z
 9228      * '&#92;u00DF' '&#92;u00E0' '&#92;u00E1' '&#92;u00E2' '&#92;u00E3' '&#92;u00E4' '&#92;u00E5' '&#92;u00E6'
 9229      * '&#92;u00E7' '&#92;u00E8' '&#92;u00E9' '&#92;u00EA' '&#92;u00EB' '&#92;u00EC' '&#92;u00ED' '&#92;u00EE'
 9230      * '&#92;u00EF' '&#92;u00F0' '&#92;u00F1' '&#92;u00F2' '&#92;u00F3' '&#92;u00F4' '&#92;u00F5' '&#92;u00F6'
 9231      * '&#92;u00F8' '&#92;u00F9' '&#92;u00FA' '&#92;u00FB' '&#92;u00FC' '&#92;u00FD' '&#92;u00FE' '&#92;u00FF'
 9232      * </pre></blockquote>
 9233      * <p> Many other Unicode characters are lowercase too.
 9234      *
 9235      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9236      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9237      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9238      * the {@link #isLowerCase(int)} method.
 9239      *
 9240      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9241      * @return  {@code true} if the character is lowercase;
 9242      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9243      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
 9244      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(char)
 9245      * @see     Character#toLowerCase(char)
 9246      * @see     Character#getType(char)
 9247      */
 9248     public static boolean isLowerCase(char ch) {
 9249         return isLowerCase((int)ch);
 9250     }

 9252     /**
 9253      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a
 9254      * lowercase character.
 9255      * <p>
 9256      * A character is lowercase if its general category type, provided
 9257      * by {@link Character#getType getType(codePoint)}, is
 9258      * {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}, or it has contributory property
 9259      * Other_Lowercase as defined by the Unicode Standard.
 9260      * <p>
 9261      * The following are examples of lowercase characters:
 9262      * <blockquote><pre>
 9263      * a b c d e f g h i j k l m n o p q r s t u v w x y z
 9264      * '&#92;u00DF' '&#92;u00E0' '&#92;u00E1' '&#92;u00E2' '&#92;u00E3' '&#92;u00E4' '&#92;u00E5' '&#92;u00E6'
 9265      * '&#92;u00E7' '&#92;u00E8' '&#92;u00E9' '&#92;u00EA' '&#92;u00EB' '&#92;u00EC' '&#92;u00ED' '&#92;u00EE'
 9266      * '&#92;u00EF' '&#92;u00F0' '&#92;u00F1' '&#92;u00F2' '&#92;u00F3' '&#92;u00F4' '&#92;u00F5' '&#92;u00F6'
 9267      * '&#92;u00F8' '&#92;u00F9' '&#92;u00FA' '&#92;u00FB' '&#92;u00FC' '&#92;u00FD' '&#92;u00FE' '&#92;u00FF'
 9268      * </pre></blockquote>
 9269      * <p> Many other Unicode characters are lowercase too.
 9270      *
 9271      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9272      * @return  {@code true} if the character is lowercase;
 9273      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9274      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(int)
 9275      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(int)
 9276      * @see     Character#toLowerCase(int)
 9277      * @see     Character#getType(int)
 9278      * @since   1.5
 9279      */
 9280     public static boolean isLowerCase(int codePoint) {
 9281         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).isLowerCase(codePoint) ||
 9282                CharacterData.of(codePoint).isOtherLowercase(codePoint);
 9283     }

 9296      * '&#92;u00C8' '&#92;u00C9' '&#92;u00CA' '&#92;u00CB' '&#92;u00CC' '&#92;u00CD' '&#92;u00CE' '&#92;u00CF'

 9313      * @see     Character#getType(char)

 9316     public static boolean isUpperCase(char ch) {

 9333      * '&#92;u00D9' '&#92;u00DA' '&#92;u00DB' '&#92;u00DC' '&#92;u00DD' '&#92;u00DE'

 9351     /**
 9352      * Determines if the specified character is a titlecase character.
 9353      * <p>
 9354      * A character is a titlecase character if its general
 9355      * category type, provided by {@code Character.getType(ch)},
 9356      * is {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}.
 9357      * <p>
 9358      * Some characters look like pairs of Latin letters. For example, there
 9359      * is an uppercase letter that looks like "LJ" and has a corresponding
 9360      * lowercase letter that looks like "lj". A third form, which looks like "Lj",
 9361      * is the appropriate form to use when rendering a word in lowercase
 9362      * with initial capitals, as for a book title.
 9363      * <p>
 9364      * These are some of the Unicode characters for which this method returns
 9365      * {@code true}:
 9366      * <ul>
 9367      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER D WITH SMALL LETTER Z WITH CARON}
 9368      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER L WITH SMALL LETTER J}
 9369      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER N WITH SMALL LETTER J}
 9370      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER D WITH SMALL LETTER Z}
 9371      * </ul>
 9372      * <p> Many other Unicode characters are titlecase too.
 9373      *
 9374      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9375      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9376      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9377      * the {@link #isTitleCase(int)} method.
 9378      *
 9379      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9380      * @return  {@code true} if the character is titlecase;
 9381      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9382      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
 9383      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(char)
 9384      * @see     Character#toTitleCase(char)
 9385      * @see     Character#getType(char)
 9386      * @since   1.0.2
 9387      */
 9388     public static boolean isTitleCase(char ch) {
 9389         return isTitleCase((int)ch);
 9390     }
 9391 
 9392     /**
 9393      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a titlecase character.
 9394      * <p>
 9395      * A character is a titlecase character if its general
 9396      * category type, provided by {@link Character#getType(int) getType(codePoint)},
 9397      * is {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}.
 9398      * <p>
 9399      * Some characters look like pairs of Latin letters. For example, there
 9400      * is an uppercase letter that looks like "LJ" and has a corresponding
 9401      * lowercase letter that looks like "lj". A third form, which looks like "Lj",
 9402      * is the appropriate form to use when rendering a word in lowercase
 9403      * with initial capitals, as for a book title.
 9404      * <p>
 9405      * These are some of the Unicode characters for which this method returns
 9406      * {@code true}:
 9407      * <ul>
 9408      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER D WITH SMALL LETTER Z WITH CARON}
 9409      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER L WITH SMALL LETTER J}
 9410      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER N WITH SMALL LETTER J}
 9411      * <li>{@code LATIN CAPITAL LETTER D WITH SMALL LETTER Z}
 9412      * </ul>
 9413      * <p> Many other Unicode characters are titlecase too.
 9414      *
 9415      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9416      * @return  {@code true} if the character is titlecase;
 9417      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9418      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(int)
 9419      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(int)
 9420      * @see     Character#toTitleCase(int)
 9421      * @see     Character#getType(int)
 9422      * @since   1.5
 9423      */
 9424     public static boolean isTitleCase(int codePoint) {
 9425         return getType(codePoint) == Character.TITLECASE_LETTER;
 9426     }

 9428     /**
 9429      * Determines if the specified character is a digit.
 9430      * <p>
 9431      * A character is a digit if its general category type, provided
 9432      * by {@code Character.getType(ch)}, is
 9433      * {@code DECIMAL_DIGIT_NUMBER}.
 9434      * <p>
 9435      * Some Unicode character ranges that contain digits:
 9436      * <ul>
 9437      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0030'} through {@code '\u005Cu0039'},
 9438      *     ISO-LATIN-1 digits ({@code '0'} through {@code '9'})
 9439      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0660'} through {@code '\u005Cu0669'},
 9440      *     Arabic-Indic digits
 9441      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu06F0'} through {@code '\u005Cu06F9'},
 9442      *     Extended Arabic-Indic digits
 9443      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0966'} through {@code '\u005Cu096F'},
 9444      *     Devanagari digits
 9445      * <li>{@code '\u005CuFF10'} through {@code '\u005CuFF19'},
 9446      *     Fullwidth digits
 9447      * </ul>
 9448      *
 9449      * Many other character ranges contain digits as well.
 9450      *
 9451      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9452      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9453      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9454      * the {@link #isDigit(int)} method.
 9455      *
 9456      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9457      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a digit;
 9458      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9459      * @see     Character#digit(char, int)
 9460      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
 9461      * @see     Character#getType(char)
 9462      */
 9463     public static boolean isDigit(char ch) {
 9464         return isDigit((int)ch);
 9465     }

 9468      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a digit.
 9469      * <p>
 9470      * A character is a digit if its general category type, provided
 9471      * by {@link Character#getType(int) getType(codePoint)}, is
 9472      * {@code DECIMAL_DIGIT_NUMBER}.
 9473      * <p>
 9474      * Some Unicode character ranges that contain digits:
 9475      * <ul>

 9501     /**
 9502      * Determines if a character is defined in Unicode.
 9503      * <p>
 9504      * A character is defined if at least one of the following is true:
 9505      * <ul>
 9506      * <li>It has an entry in the UnicodeData file.
 9507      * <li>It has a value in a range defined by the UnicodeData file.
 9508      * </ul>
 9509      *
 9510      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9511      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9512      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9513      * the {@link #isDefined(int)} method.
 9514      *
 9515      * @param   ch   the character to be tested
 9516      * @return  {@code true} if the character has a defined meaning
 9517      *          in Unicode; {@code false} otherwise.
 9518      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
 9519      * @see     Character#isLetter(char)
 9520      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(char)
 9521      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
 9522      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(char)
 9523      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(char)
 9524      * @since   1.0.2
 9525      */
 9526     public static boolean isDefined(char ch) {
 9527         return isDefined((int)ch);
 9528     }
