 9530     /**
 9531      * Determines if a character (Unicode code point) is defined in Unicode.
 9532      * <p>
 9533      * A character is defined if at least one of the following is true:
 9534      * <ul>
 9535      * <li>It has an entry in the UnicodeData file.
 9536      * <li>It has a value in a range defined by the UnicodeData file.
 9537      * </ul>
 9538      *
 9539      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9540      * @return  {@code true} if the character has a defined meaning
 9541      *          in Unicode; {@code false} otherwise.
 9542      * @see     Character#isDigit(int)
 9543      * @see     Character#isLetter(int)
 9544      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(int)
 9545      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(int)
 9546      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(int)
 9547      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(int)
 9548      * @since   1.5
 9549      */
 9550     public static boolean isDefined(int codePoint) {
 9551         return getType(codePoint) != Character.UNASSIGNED;
 9552     }
 9553 
 9554     /**
 9555      * Determines if the specified character is a letter.
 9556      * <p>
 9557      * A character is considered to be a letter if its general
 9558      * category type, provided by {@code Character.getType(ch)},
 9559      * is any of the following:
 9560      * <ul>
 9561      * <li> {@code UPPERCASE_LETTER}
 9562      * <li> {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}
 9563      * <li> {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}
 9564      * <li> {@code MODIFIER_LETTER}
 9565      * <li> {@code OTHER_LETTER}
 9566      * </ul>
 9567      *
 9568      * Not all letters have case. Many characters are
 9569      * letters but are neither uppercase nor lowercase nor titlecase.
 9570      *
 9571      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9572      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9573      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9574      * the {@link #isLetter(int)} method.
 9575      *
 9576      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9577      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a letter;
 9578      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9579      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
 9580      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(char)
 9581      * @see     Character#isJavaLetter(char)
 9582      * @see     Character#isJavaLetterOrDigit(char)
 9583      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(char)
 9584      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
 9585      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(char)
 9586      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierStart(char)
 9587      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(char)
 9588      */
 9589     public static boolean isLetter(char ch) {
 9590         return isLetter((int)ch);
 9591     }
 9592 
 9593     /**
 9594      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a letter.
 9595      * <p>
 9596      * A character is considered to be a letter if its general
 9597      * category type, provided by {@link Character#getType(int) getType(codePoint)},
 9598      * is any of the following:
 9599      * <ul>
 9600      * <li> {@code UPPERCASE_LETTER}
 9601      * <li> {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}
 9602      * <li> {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}
 9603      * <li> {@code MODIFIER_LETTER}
 9604      * <li> {@code OTHER_LETTER}
 9605      * </ul>
 9606      *
 9607      * Not all letters have case. Many characters are
 9608      * letters but are neither uppercase nor lowercase nor titlecase.
 9609      *
 9610      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9611      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a letter;
 9612      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9613      * @see     Character#isDigit(int)
 9614      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(int)
 9615      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(int)
 9616      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(int)
 9617      * @see     Character#isTitleCase(int)
 9618      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierStart(int)
 9619      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(int)
 9620      * @since   1.5
 9621      */
 9622     public static boolean isLetter(int codePoint) {
 9623         return ((((1 << Character.UPPERCASE_LETTER) |
 9624             (1 << Character.LOWERCASE_LETTER) |
 9625             (1 << Character.TITLECASE_LETTER) |
 9626             (1 << Character.MODIFIER_LETTER) |
 9627             (1 << Character.OTHER_LETTER)) >> getType(codePoint)) & 1)
 9628             != 0;
 9629     }
 9630 
 9631     /**
 9632      * Determines if the specified character is a letter or digit.
 9633      * <p>
 9634      * A character is considered to be a letter or digit if either
 9635      * {@code Character.isLetter(char ch)} or
 9636      * {@code Character.isDigit(char ch)} returns
 9637      * {@code true} for the character.
 9638      *
 9639      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
 9640      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
 9641      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
 9642      * the {@link #isLetterOrDigit(int)} method.
 9643      *
 9644      * @param   ch   the character to be tested.
 9645      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a letter or digit;
 9646      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9647      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
 9648      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(char)
 9649      * @see     Character#isJavaLetter(char)
 9650      * @see     Character#isJavaLetterOrDigit(char)
 9651      * @see     Character#isLetter(char)
 9652      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierPart(char)
 9653      * @since   1.0.2
 9654      */
 9655     public static boolean isLetterOrDigit(char ch) {
 9656         return isLetterOrDigit((int)ch);
 9657     }
 9658 
 9659     /**
 9660      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a letter or digit.
 9661      * <p>
 9662      * A character is considered to be a letter or digit if either
 9663      * {@link #isLetter(int) isLetter(codePoint)} or
 9664      * {@link #isDigit(int) isDigit(codePoint)} returns
 9665      * {@code true} for the character.
 9666      *
 9667      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9668      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a letter or digit;
 9669      *          {@code false} otherwise.
 9670      * @see     Character#isDigit(int)
 9671      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(int)
 9672      * @see     Character#isLetter(int)
 9673      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierPart(int)
 9674      * @since   1.5
 9675      */
 9676     public static boolean isLetterOrDigit(int codePoint) {
 9677         return ((((1 << Character.UPPERCASE_LETTER) |
 9678             (1 << Character.LOWERCASE_LETTER) |
 9679             (1 << Character.TITLECASE_LETTER) |
 9680             (1 << Character.MODIFIER_LETTER) |
 9681             (1 << Character.OTHER_LETTER) |
 9682             (1 << Character.DECIMAL_DIGIT_NUMBER)) >> getType(codePoint)) & 1)
 9683             != 0;
 9684     }

 9686     /**
 9687      * Determines if the specified character is permissible as the first
 9688      * character in a Java identifier.
 9689      * <p>
 9690      * A character may start a Java identifier if and only if
 9691      * one of the following conditions is true:
 9692      * <ul>
 9693      * <li> {@link #isLetter(char) isLetter(ch)} returns {@code true}
 9694      * <li> {@link #getType(char) getType(ch)} returns {@code LETTER_NUMBER}
 9695      * <li> {@code ch} is a currency symbol (such as {@code '$'})
 9696      * <li> {@code ch} is a connecting punctuation character (such as {@code '_'}).
 9697      * </ul>
 9698      *
 9699      * @param   ch the character to be tested.
 9700      * @return  {@code true} if the character may start a Java
 9701      *          identifier; {@code false} otherwise.
 9702      * @see     Character#isJavaLetterOrDigit(char)
 9703      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(char)
 9704      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(char)
 9705      * @see     Character#isLetter(char)
 9706      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(char)
 9707      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierStart(char)
 9708      * @since   1.0.2
 9709      * @deprecated Replaced by isJavaIdentifierStart(char).
 9710      */
 9711     @Deprecated(since="1.1")
 9712     public static boolean isJavaLetter(char ch) {
 9713         return isJavaIdentifierStart(ch);
 9714     }

 9716     /**
 9717      * Determines if the specified character may be part of a Java
 9718      * identifier as other than the first character.
 9719      * <p>
 9720      * A character may be part of a Java identifier if and only if one
 9721      * of the following conditions is true:
 9722      * <ul>
 9723      * <li>  it is a letter
 9724      * <li>  it is a currency symbol (such as {@code '$'})
 9725      * <li>  it is a connecting punctuation character (such as {@code '_'})
 9726      * <li>  it is a digit
 9727      * <li>  it is a numeric letter (such as a Roman numeral character)
 9728      * <li>  it is a combining mark
 9729      * <li>  it is a non-spacing mark
 9730      * <li> {@code isIdentifierIgnorable} returns
 9731      * {@code true} for the character.
 9732      * </ul>
 9733      *
 9734      * @param   ch the character to be tested.
 9735      * @return  {@code true} if the character may be part of a
 9736      *          Java identifier; {@code false} otherwise.
 9737      * @see     Character#isJavaLetter(char)
 9738      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierStart(char)
 9739      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(char)
 9740      * @see     Character#isLetter(char)
 9741      * @see     Character#isLetterOrDigit(char)
 9742      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierPart(char)
 9743      * @see     Character#isIdentifierIgnorable(char)
 9744      * @since   1.0.2
 9745      * @deprecated Replaced by isJavaIdentifierPart(char).
 9746      */
 9747     @Deprecated(since="1.1")
 9748     public static boolean isJavaLetterOrDigit(char ch) {
 9749         return isJavaIdentifierPart(ch);
 9750     }
 9751 
 9752     /**
 9753      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is alphabetic.
 9754      * <p>
 9755      * A character is considered to be alphabetic if its general category type,
 9756      * provided by {@link Character#getType(int) getType(codePoint)}, is any of
 9757      * the following:
 9758      * <ul>
 9759      * <li> {@code UPPERCASE_LETTER}
 9760      * <li> {@code LOWERCASE_LETTER}
 9761      * <li> {@code TITLECASE_LETTER}
 9762      * <li> {@code MODIFIER_LETTER}
 9763      * <li> {@code OTHER_LETTER}
 9764      * <li> {@code LETTER_NUMBER}
 9765      * </ul>
 9766      * or it has contributory property Other_Alphabetic as defined by the
 9767      * Unicode Standard.
 9768      *
 9769      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
 9770      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a Unicode alphabet
 9771      *          character, {@code false} otherwise.
 9772      * @since   1.7
 9773      */
 9774     public static boolean isAlphabetic(int codePoint) {
 9775         return (((((1 << Character.UPPERCASE_LETTER) |
 9776             (1 << Character.LOWERCASE_LETTER) |
 9777             (1 << Character.TITLECASE_LETTER) |
 9778             (1 << Character.MODIFIER_LETTER) |
 9779             (1 << Character.OTHER_LETTER) |
 9780             (1 << Character.LETTER_NUMBER)) >> getType(codePoint)) & 1) != 0) ||
 9781             CharacterData.of(codePoint).isOtherAlphabetic(codePoint);
 9782     }

10099     /**
10100      * Determines if the specified character should be regarded as
10101      * an ignorable character in a Java identifier or a Unicode identifier.
10102      * <p>
10103      * The following Unicode characters are ignorable in a Java identifier
10104      * or a Unicode identifier:
10105      * <ul>
10106      * <li>ISO control characters that are not whitespace
10107      * <ul>
10108      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu0000'} through {@code '\u005Cu0008'}
10109      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu000E'} through {@code '\u005Cu001B'}
10110      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu007F'} through {@code '\u005Cu009F'}
10111      * </ul>
10112      *
10113      * <li>all characters that have the {@code FORMAT} general
10114      * category value
10115      * </ul>
10116      *
10117      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10118      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10119      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10120      * the {@link #isIdentifierIgnorable(int)} method.
10121      *
10122      * @param   ch      the character to be tested.
10123      * @return  {@code true} if the character is an ignorable control
10124      *          character that may be part of a Java or Unicode identifier;
10125      *           {@code false} otherwise.
10126      * @see     Character#isJavaIdentifierPart(char)
10127      * @see     Character#isUnicodeIdentifierPart(char)
10128      * @since   1.1
10129      */

10131         return isIdentifierIgnorable((int)ch);
10132     }

10139      * or a Unicode identifier:

10145      * <li>{@code '\u005Cu007F'} through {@code '\u005Cu009F'}

10149      * category value

10164     /**
10165      * Converts the character argument to lowercase using case
10166      * mapping information from the UnicodeData file.
10167      * <p>
10168      * Note that
10169      * {@code Character.isLowerCase(Character.toLowerCase(ch))}
10170      * does not always return {@code true} for some ranges of
10171      * characters, particularly those that are symbols or ideographs.
10172      *
10173      * <p>In general, {@link String#toLowerCase()} should be used to map
10174      * characters to lowercase. {@code String} case mapping methods
10175      * have several benefits over {@code Character} case mapping methods.
10176      * {@code String} case mapping methods can perform locale-sensitive
10177      * mappings, context-sensitive mappings, and 1:M character mappings, whereas
10178      * the {@code Character} case mapping methods cannot.
10179      *
10180      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10181      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10182      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10183      * the {@link #toLowerCase(int)} method.
10184      *
10185      * @param   ch   the character to be converted.
10186      * @return  the lowercase equivalent of the character, if any;
10187      *          otherwise, the character itself.
10188      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
10189      * @see     String#toLowerCase()
10190      */
10191     public static char toLowerCase(char ch) {
10192         return (char)toLowerCase((int)ch);
10193     }

10343     /**
10344      * Returns the numeric value of the character {@code ch} in the
10345      * specified radix.
10346      * <p>
10347      * If the radix is not in the range {@code MIN_RADIX} &le;
10348      * {@code radix} &le; {@code MAX_RADIX} or if the
10349      * value of {@code ch} is not a valid digit in the specified
10350      * radix, {@code -1} is returned. A character is a valid digit
10351      * if at least one of the following is true:
10352      * <ul>
10353      * <li>The method {@code isDigit} is {@code true} of the character
10354      *     and the Unicode decimal digit value of the character (or its
10355      *     single-character decomposition) is less than the specified radix.
10356      *     In this case the decimal digit value is returned.
10357      * <li>The character is one of the uppercase Latin letters
10358      *     {@code 'A'} through {@code 'Z'} and its code is less than
10359      *     {@code radix + 'A' - 10}.
10360      *     In this case, {@code ch - 'A' + 10}
10361      *     is returned.
10362      * <li>The character is one of the lowercase Latin letters
10363      *     {@code 'a'} through {@code 'z'} and its code is less than
10364      *     {@code radix + 'a' - 10}.
10365      *     In this case, {@code ch - 'a' + 10}
10366      *     is returned.
10367      * <li>The character is one of the fullwidth uppercase Latin letters A
10368      *     ({@code '\u005CuFF21'}) through Z ({@code '\u005CuFF3A'})
10369      *     and its code is less than
10370      *     {@code radix + '\u005CuFF21' - 10}.
10371      *     In this case, {@code ch - '\u005CuFF21' + 10}
10372      *     is returned.
10373      * <li>The character is one of the fullwidth lowercase Latin letters a
10374      *     ({@code '\u005CuFF41'}) through z ({@code '\u005CuFF5A'})
10375      *     and its code is less than
10376      *     {@code radix + '\u005CuFF41' - 10}.
10377      *     In this case, {@code ch - '\u005CuFF41' + 10}
10378      *     is returned.
10379      * </ul>
10380      *
10381      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10382      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10383      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10384      * the {@link #digit(int, int)} method.
10385      *
10386      * @param   ch      the character to be converted.
10387      * @param   radix   the radix.
10388      * @return  the numeric value represented by the character in the
10389      *          specified radix.
10390      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
10391      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
10392      */
10393     public static int digit(char ch, int radix) {
10394         return digit((int)ch, radix);
10395     }
10396 
10397     /**
10398      * Returns the numeric value of the specified character (Unicode
10399      * code point) in the specified radix.
10400      *
10401      * <p>If the radix is not in the range {@code MIN_RADIX} &le;
10402      * {@code radix} &le; {@code MAX_RADIX} or if the
10403      * character is not a valid digit in the specified
10404      * radix, {@code -1} is returned. A character is a valid digit
10405      * if at least one of the following is true:
10406      * <ul>
10407      * <li>The method {@link #isDigit(int) isDigit(codePoint)} is {@code true} of the character
10408      *     and the Unicode decimal digit value of the character (or its
10409      *     single-character decomposition) is less than the specified radix.
10410      *     In this case the decimal digit value is returned.
10411      * <li>The character is one of the uppercase Latin letters
10412      *     {@code 'A'} through {@code 'Z'} and its code is less than
10413      *     {@code radix + 'A' - 10}.
10414      *     In this case, {@code codePoint - 'A' + 10}
10415      *     is returned.
10416      * <li>The character is one of the lowercase Latin letters
10417      *     {@code 'a'} through {@code 'z'} and its code is less than
10418      *     {@code radix + 'a' - 10}.
10419      *     In this case, {@code codePoint - 'a' + 10}
10420      *     is returned.
10421      * <li>The character is one of the fullwidth uppercase Latin letters A
10422      *     ({@code '\u005CuFF21'}) through Z ({@code '\u005CuFF3A'})
10423      *     and its code is less than
10424      *     {@code radix + '\u005CuFF21' - 10}.
10425      *     In this case,
10426      *     {@code codePoint - '\u005CuFF21' + 10}
10427      *     is returned.
10428      * <li>The character is one of the fullwidth lowercase Latin letters a
10429      *     ({@code '\u005CuFF41'}) through z ({@code '\u005CuFF5A'})
10430      *     and its code is less than
10431      *     {@code radix + '\u005CuFF41'- 10}.
10432      *     In this case,
10433      *     {@code codePoint - '\u005CuFF41' + 10}
10434      *     is returned.
10435      * </ul>
10436      *
10437      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be converted.
10438      * @param   radix   the radix.
10439      * @return  the numeric value represented by the character in the
10440      *          specified radix.
10441      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
10442      * @see     Character#isDigit(int)
10443      * @since   1.5
10444      */
10445     public static int digit(int codePoint, int radix) {
10446         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).digit(codePoint, radix);
10447     }

10449     /**
10450      * Returns the {@code int} value that the specified Unicode
10451      * character represents. For example, the character
10452      * {@code '\u005Cu216C'} (the roman numeral fifty) will return
10453      * an int with a value of 50.
10454      * <p>
10455      * The letters A-Z in their uppercase ({@code '\u005Cu0041'} through
10456      * {@code '\u005Cu005A'}), lowercase
10457      * ({@code '\u005Cu0061'} through {@code '\u005Cu007A'}), and
10458      * full width variant ({@code '\u005CuFF21'} through
10459      * {@code '\u005CuFF3A'} and {@code '\u005CuFF41'} through
10460      * {@code '\u005CuFF5A'}) forms have numeric values from 10
10461      * through 35. This is independent of the Unicode specification,
10462      * which does not assign numeric values to these {@code char}
10463      * values.
10464      * <p>
10465      * If the character does not have a numeric value, then -1 is returned.
10466      * If the character has a numeric value that cannot be represented as a
10467      * nonnegative integer (for example, a fractional value), then -2
10468      * is returned.
10469      *
10470      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10471      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10472      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10473      * the {@link #getNumericValue(int)} method.
10474      *
10475      * @param   ch      the character to be converted.
10476      * @return  the numeric value of the character, as a nonnegative {@code int}
10477      *          value; -2 if the character has a numeric value but the value
10478      *          can not be represented as a nonnegative {@code int} value;
10479      *          -1 if the character has no numeric value.
10480      * @see     Character#forDigit(int, int)
10481      * @see     Character#isDigit(char)
10482      * @since   1.1
10483      */
10484     public static int getNumericValue(char ch) {
10485         return getNumericValue((int)ch);
10486     }
10487 
10488     /**
10489      * Returns the {@code int} value that the specified
10490      * character (Unicode code point) represents. For example, the character
10491      * {@code '\u005Cu216C'} (the Roman numeral fifty) will return
10492      * an {@code int} with a value of 50.
10493      * <p>
10494      * The letters A-Z in their uppercase ({@code '\u005Cu0041'} through
10495      * {@code '\u005Cu005A'}), lowercase
10496      * ({@code '\u005Cu0061'} through {@code '\u005Cu007A'}), and
10497      * full width variant ({@code '\u005CuFF21'} through
10498      * {@code '\u005CuFF3A'} and {@code '\u005CuFF41'} through
10499      * {@code '\u005CuFF5A'}) forms have numeric values from 10
10500      * through 35. This is independent of the Unicode specification,
10501      * which does not assign numeric values to these {@code char}
10502      * values.
10503      * <p>
10504      * If the character does not have a numeric value, then -1 is returned.

10522     /**
10523      * Determines if the specified character is ISO-LATIN-1 white space.
10524      * This method returns {@code true} for the following five
10525      * characters only:
10526      * <table class="striped">
10527      * <caption style="display:none">truechars</caption>
10528      * <thead>
10529      * <tr><th scope="col">Character
10530      *     <th scope="col">Code
10531      *     <th scope="col">Name
10532      * </thead>
10533      * <tbody>
10534      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code '\t'}</th>            <td>{@code U+0009}</td>
10535      *     <td>{@code HORIZONTAL TABULATION}</td></tr>
10536      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code '\n'}</th>            <td>{@code U+000A}</td>
10537      *     <td>{@code NEW LINE}</td></tr>
10538      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code '\f'}</th>            <td>{@code U+000C}</td>
10539      *     <td>{@code FORM FEED}</td></tr>
10540      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code '\r'}</th>            <td>{@code U+000D}</td>
10541      *     <td>{@code CARRIAGE RETURN}</td></tr>
10542      * <tr><th scope="row">{@code ' '}</th>  <td>{@code U+0020}</td>
10543      *     <td>{@code SPACE}</td></tr>
10544      * </tbody>
10545      * </table>
10546      *
10547      * @param      ch   the character to be tested.
10548      * @return     {@code true} if the character is ISO-LATIN-1 white
10549      *             space; {@code false} otherwise.
10550      * @see        Character#isSpaceChar(char)
10551      * @see        Character#isWhitespace(char)
10552      * @deprecated Replaced by isWhitespace(char).
10553      */
10554     @Deprecated(since="1.1")
10555     public static boolean isSpace(char ch) {
10556         return (ch <= 0x0020) &&
10557             (((((1L << 0x0009) |
10558             (1L << 0x000A) |
10559             (1L << 0x000C) |
10560             (1L << 0x000D) |
10561             (1L << 0x0020)) >> ch) & 1L) != 0);
10562     }

10565     /**
10566      * Determines if the specified character is a Unicode space character.
10567      * A character is considered to be a space character if and only if
10568      * it is specified to be a space character by the Unicode Standard. This
10569      * method returns true if the character's general category type is any of
10570      * the following:
10571      * <ul>
10572      * <li> {@code SPACE_SEPARATOR}
10573      * <li> {@code LINE_SEPARATOR}
10574      * <li> {@code PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR}
10575      * </ul>
10576      *
10577      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10578      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10579      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10580      * the {@link #isSpaceChar(int)} method.
10581      *
10582      * @param   ch      the character to be tested.
10583      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a space character;
10584      *          {@code false} otherwise.
10585      * @see     Character#isWhitespace(char)
10586      * @since   1.1
10587      */
10588     public static boolean isSpaceChar(char ch) {
10589         return isSpaceChar((int)ch);
10590     }
10591 
10592     /**
10593      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is a
10594      * Unicode space character.  A character is considered to be a
10595      * space character if and only if it is specified to be a space
10596      * character by the Unicode Standard. This method returns true if
10597      * the character's general category type is any of the following:
10598      *
10599      * <ul>
10600      * <li> {@link #SPACE_SEPARATOR}
10601      * <li> {@link #LINE_SEPARATOR}
10602      * <li> {@link #PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR}
10603      * </ul>
10604      *
10605      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
10606      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a space character;
10607      *          {@code false} otherwise.
10608      * @see     Character#isWhitespace(int)
10609      * @since   1.5
10610      */
10611     public static boolean isSpaceChar(int codePoint) {
10612         return ((((1 << Character.SPACE_SEPARATOR) |
10613                   (1 << Character.LINE_SEPARATOR) |
10614                   (1 << Character.PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR)) >> getType(codePoint)) & 1)
10615             != 0;
10616     }
10617 
10618     /**
10619      * Determines if the specified character is white space according to Java.
10620      * A character is a Java whitespace character if and only if it satisfies
10621      * one of the following criteria:
10622      * <ul>
10623      * <li> It is a Unicode space character ({@code SPACE_SEPARATOR},
10624      *      {@code LINE_SEPARATOR}, or {@code PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR})
10625      *      but is not also a non-breaking space ({@code '\u005Cu00A0'},
10626      *      {@code '\u005Cu2007'}, {@code '\u005Cu202F'}).
10627      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Ct'}, U+0009 HORIZONTAL TABULATION.
10628      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cn'}, U+000A LINE FEED.
10629      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu000B'}, U+000B VERTICAL TABULATION.
10630      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cf'}, U+000C FORM FEED.
10631      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cr'}, U+000D CARRIAGE RETURN.
10632      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001C'}, U+001C FILE SEPARATOR.
10633      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001D'}, U+001D GROUP SEPARATOR.
10634      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001E'}, U+001E RECORD SEPARATOR.
10635      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001F'}, U+001F UNIT SEPARATOR.
10636      * </ul>
10637      *
10638      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10639      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10640      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10641      * the {@link #isWhitespace(int)} method.
10642      *
10643      * @param   ch the character to be tested.
10644      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a Java whitespace
10645      *          character; {@code false} otherwise.
10646      * @see     Character#isSpaceChar(char)
10647      * @since   1.1
10648      */
10649     public static boolean isWhitespace(char ch) {
10650         return isWhitespace((int)ch);
10651     }
10652 
10653     /**
10654      * Determines if the specified character (Unicode code point) is
10655      * white space according to Java.  A character is a Java
10656      * whitespace character if and only if it satisfies one of the
10657      * following criteria:
10658      * <ul>
10659      * <li> It is a Unicode space character ({@link #SPACE_SEPARATOR},
10660      *      {@link #LINE_SEPARATOR}, or {@link #PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR})
10661      *      but is not also a non-breaking space ({@code '\u005Cu00A0'},
10662      *      {@code '\u005Cu2007'}, {@code '\u005Cu202F'}).
10663      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Ct'}, U+0009 HORIZONTAL TABULATION.
10664      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cn'}, U+000A LINE FEED.
10665      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu000B'}, U+000B VERTICAL TABULATION.
10666      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cf'}, U+000C FORM FEED.
10667      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cr'}, U+000D CARRIAGE RETURN.
10668      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001C'}, U+001C FILE SEPARATOR.
10669      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001D'}, U+001D GROUP SEPARATOR.
10670      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001E'}, U+001E RECORD SEPARATOR.
10671      * <li> It is {@code '\u005Cu001F'}, U+001F UNIT SEPARATOR.
10672      * </ul>
10673      *
10674      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
10675      * @return  {@code true} if the character is a Java whitespace
10676      *          character; {@code false} otherwise.
10677      * @see     Character#isSpaceChar(int)
10678      * @since   1.5
10679      */
10680     public static boolean isWhitespace(int codePoint) {
10681         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).isWhitespace(codePoint);
10682     }
10683 
10684     /**
10685      * Determines if the specified character is an ISO control
10686      * character.  A character is considered to be an ISO control
10687      * character if its code is in the range {@code '\u005Cu0000'}
10688      * through {@code '\u005Cu001F'} or in the range
10689      * {@code '\u005Cu007F'} through {@code '\u005Cu009F'}.
10690      *
10691      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10692      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10693      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10694      * the {@link #isISOControl(int)} method.
10695      *
10696      * @param   ch      the character to be tested.
10697      * @return  {@code true} if the character is an ISO control character;
10698      *          {@code false} otherwise.
10699      *
10700      * @see     Character#isSpaceChar(char)
10701      * @see     Character#isWhitespace(char)
10702      * @since   1.1
10703      */
10704     public static boolean isISOControl(char ch) {
10705         return isISOControl((int)ch);
10706     }
10707 
10708     /**
10709      * Determines if the referenced character (Unicode code point) is an ISO control
10710      * character.  A character is considered to be an ISO control
10711      * character if its code is in the range {@code '\u005Cu0000'}
10712      * through {@code '\u005Cu001F'} or in the range
10713      * {@code '\u005Cu007F'} through {@code '\u005Cu009F'}.
10714      *
10715      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
10716      * @return  {@code true} if the character is an ISO control character;
10717      *          {@code false} otherwise.
10718      * @see     Character#isSpaceChar(int)
10719      * @see     Character#isWhitespace(int)
10720      * @since   1.5
10721      */
10722     public static boolean isISOControl(int codePoint) {
10723         // Optimized form of:
10724         //     (codePoint >= 0x00 && codePoint <= 0x1F) ||
10725         //     (codePoint >= 0x7F && codePoint <= 0x9F);
10726         return codePoint <= 0x9F &&
10727             (codePoint >= 0x7F || (codePoint >>> 5 == 0));
10728     }
10729

10731      * Returns a value indicating a character's general category.
10732      *

10792      * @see     Character#FORMAT FORMAT
10793      * @see     Character#INITIAL_QUOTE_PUNCTUATION INITIAL_QUOTE_PUNCTUATION
10794      * @see     Character#LETTER_NUMBER LETTER_NUMBER
10795      * @see     Character#LINE_SEPARATOR LINE_SEPARATOR
10796      * @see     Character#LOWERCASE_LETTER LOWERCASE_LETTER
10797      * @see     Character#MATH_SYMBOL MATH_SYMBOL
10798      * @see     Character#MODIFIER_LETTER MODIFIER_LETTER

10801      * @see     Character#OTHER_LETTER OTHER_LETTER

10804      * @see     Character#OTHER_SYMBOL OTHER_SYMBOL

10810      * @see     Character#TITLECASE_LETTER TITLECASE_LETTER

10812      * @see     Character#UPPERCASE_LETTER UPPERCASE_LETTER
10813      * @since   1.5
10814      */
10815     public static int getType(int codePoint) {
10816         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).getType(codePoint);
10817     }

10819     /**
10820      * Determines the character representation for a specific digit in
10821      * the specified radix. If the value of {@code radix} is not a
10822      * valid radix, or the value of {@code digit} is not a valid
10823      * digit in the specified radix, the null character
10824      * ({@code '\u005Cu0000'}) is returned.
10825      * <p>
10826      * The {@code radix} argument is valid if it is greater than or
10827      * equal to {@code MIN_RADIX} and less than or equal to
10828      * {@code MAX_RADIX}. The {@code digit} argument is valid if
10829      * {@code 0 <= digit < radix}.
10830      * <p>
10831      * If the digit is less than 10, then
10832      * {@code '0' + digit} is returned. Otherwise, the value
10833      * {@code 'a' + digit - 10} is returned.
10834      *
10835      * @param   digit   the number to convert to a character.
10836      * @param   radix   the radix.
10837      * @return  the {@code char} representation of the specified digit
10838      *          in the specified radix.
10839      * @see     Character#MIN_RADIX
10840      * @see     Character#MAX_RADIX
10841      * @see     Character#digit(char, int)
10842      */
10843     public static char forDigit(int digit, int radix) {
10844         if ((digit >= radix) || (digit < 0)) {
10845             return '\0';
10846         }
10847         if ((radix < Character.MIN_RADIX) || (radix > Character.MAX_RADIX)) {
10848             return '\0';
10849         }
10850         if (digit < 10) {
10851             return (char)('0' + digit);
10852         }
10853         return (char)('a' - 10 + digit);
10854     }
10855 
10856     /**
10857      * Returns the Unicode directionality property for the given
10858      * character.  Character directionality is used to calculate the
10859      * visual ordering of text. The directionality value of undefined
10860      * {@code char} values is {@code DIRECTIONALITY_UNDEFINED}.
10861      *
10862      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10863      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10864      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10865      * the {@link #getDirectionality(int)} method.
10866      *
10867      * @param  ch {@code char} for which the directionality property
10868      *            is requested.
10869      * @return the directionality property of the {@code char} value.
10870      *
10871      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_UNDEFINED
10872      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_LEFT_TO_RIGHT
10873      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_RIGHT_TO_LEFT
10874      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_RIGHT_TO_LEFT_ARABIC
10875      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_EUROPEAN_NUMBER
10876      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_EUROPEAN_NUMBER_SEPARATOR
10877      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_EUROPEAN_NUMBER_TERMINATOR
10878      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_ARABIC_NUMBER
10879      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_COMMON_NUMBER_SEPARATOR
10880      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_NONSPACING_MARK
10881      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_BOUNDARY_NEUTRAL
10882      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR
10883      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_SEGMENT_SEPARATOR

10885      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_OTHER_NEUTRALS
10886      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_LEFT_TO_RIGHT_EMBEDDING
10887      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_LEFT_TO_RIGHT_OVERRIDE
10888      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_RIGHT_TO_LEFT_EMBEDDING
10889      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_RIGHT_TO_LEFT_OVERRIDE
10890      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_POP_DIRECTIONAL_FORMAT
10891      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_LEFT_TO_RIGHT_ISOLATE
10892      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_RIGHT_TO_LEFT_ISOLATE
10893      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_FIRST_STRONG_ISOLATE
10894      * @see Character#DIRECTIONALITY_POP_DIRECTIONAL_ISOLATE
10895      * @since 1.4
10896      */
10897     public static byte getDirectionality(char ch) {

10942     /**
10943      * Determines whether the character is mirrored according to the
10944      * Unicode specification.  Mirrored characters should have their
10945      * glyphs horizontally mirrored when displayed in text that is
10946      * right-to-left.  For example, {@code '\u005Cu0028'} LEFT
10947      * PARENTHESIS is semantically defined to be an <i>opening
10948      * parenthesis</i>.  This will appear as a "(" in text that is
10949      * left-to-right but as a ")" in text that is right-to-left.
10950      *
10951      * <p><b>Note:</b> This method cannot handle <a
10952      * href="#supplementary"> supplementary characters</a>. To support
10953      * all Unicode characters, including supplementary characters, use
10954      * the {@link #isMirrored(int)} method.
10955      *
10956      * @param  ch {@code char} for which the mirrored property is requested
10957      * @return {@code true} if the char is mirrored, {@code false}
10958      *         if the {@code char} is not mirrored or is not defined.
10959      * @since 1.4
10960      */
10961     public static boolean isMirrored(char ch) {
10962         return isMirrored((int)ch);
10963     }
10964 
10965     /**
10966      * Determines whether the specified character (Unicode code point)
10967      * is mirrored according to the Unicode specification.  Mirrored
10968      * characters should have their glyphs horizontally mirrored when
10969      * displayed in text that is right-to-left.  For example,
10970      * {@code '\u005Cu0028'} LEFT PARENTHESIS is semantically
10971      * defined to be an <i>opening parenthesis</i>.  This will appear
10972      * as a "(" in text that is left-to-right but as a ")" in text
10973      * that is right-to-left.
10974      *
10975      * @param   codePoint the character (Unicode code point) to be tested.
10976      * @return  {@code true} if the character is mirrored, {@code false}
10977      *          if the character is not mirrored or is not defined.
10978      * @since   1.5
10979      */
10980     public static boolean isMirrored(int codePoint) {
10981         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).isMirrored(codePoint);
10982     }

10984     /**
10985      * Compares two {@code Character} objects numerically.
10986      *
10987      * @param   anotherCharacter   the {@code Character} to be compared.
10988      * @return  the value {@code 0} if the argument {@code Character}
10989      *          is equal to this {@code Character}; a value less than
10990      *          {@code 0} if this {@code Character} is numerically less
10991      *          than the {@code Character} argument; and a value greater than
10992      *          {@code 0} if this {@code Character} is numerically greater
10993      *          than the {@code Character} argument (unsigned comparison).
10994      *          Note that this is strictly a numerical comparison; it is not
10995      *          locale-dependent.
10996      * @since   1.2
10997      */
10998     public int compareTo(Character anotherCharacter) {
10999         return compare(this.value, anotherCharacter.value);
11000     }

11002     /**
11003      * Compares two {@code char} values numerically.
11004      * The value returned is identical to what would be returned by:
11005      * <pre>
11006      *    Character.valueOf(x).compareTo(Character.valueOf(y))
11007      * </pre>
11008      *
11009      * @param  x the first {@code char} to compare
11010      * @param  y the second {@code char} to compare
11011      * @return the value {@code 0} if {@code x == y};
11012      *         a value less than {@code 0} if {@code x < y}; and
11013      *         a value greater than {@code 0} if {@code x > y}
11014      * @since 1.7
11015      */
11016     public static int compare(char x, char y) {
11017         return x - y;
11018     }

11020     /**
11021      * Converts the character (Unicode code point) argument to uppercase using
11022      * information from the UnicodeData file.
11023      *
11024      * @param   codePoint   the character (Unicode code point) to be converted.
11025      * @return  either the uppercase equivalent of the character, if
11026      *          any, or an error flag ({@code Character.ERROR})
11027      *          that indicates that a 1:M {@code char} mapping exists.
11028      * @see     Character#isLowerCase(char)
11029      * @see     Character#isUpperCase(char)
11030      * @see     Character#toLowerCase(char)
11031      * @see     Character#toTitleCase(char)
11032      * @since 1.4
11033      */
11034     static int toUpperCaseEx(int codePoint) {
11035         assert isValidCodePoint(codePoint);
11036         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).toUpperCaseEx(codePoint);
11037     }
11038 
11039     /**
11040      * Converts the character (Unicode code point) argument to uppercase using case
11041      * mapping information from the SpecialCasing file in the Unicode
11042      * specification. If a character has no explicit uppercase
11043      * mapping, then the {@code char} itself is returned in the
11044      * {@code char[]}.
11045      *
11046      * @param   codePoint   the character (Unicode code point) to be converted.
11047      * @return a {@code char[]} with the uppercased character.
11048      * @since 1.4
11049      */
11050     static char[] toUpperCaseCharArray(int codePoint) {
11051         // As of Unicode 6.0, 1:M uppercasings only happen in the BMP.
11052         assert isBmpCodePoint(codePoint);
11053         return CharacterData.of(codePoint).toUpperCaseCharArray(codePoint);
11054     }

11056     /**
11057      * The number of bits used to represent a {@code char} value in unsigned
11058      * binary form, constant {@code 16}.
11059      *
11060      * @since 1.5
11061      */
11062     public static final int SIZE = 16;
11063 
11064     /**
11065      * The number of bytes used to represent a {@code char} value in unsigned
11066      * binary form.
11067      *
11068      * @since 1.8
11069      */
11070     public static final int BYTES = SIZE / Byte.SIZE;
11071 
11072     /**
11073      * Returns the value obtained by reversing the order of the bytes in the
11074      * specified {@code char} value.
11075      *
11076      * @param ch The {@code char} of which to reverse the byte order.
11077      * @return the value obtained by reversing (or, equivalently, swapping)
11078      *     the bytes in the specified {@code char} value.
11079      * @since 1.5
11080      */
11081     @HotSpotIntrinsicCandidate
11082     public static char reverseBytes(char ch) {
11083         return (char) (((ch & 0xFF00) >> 8) | (ch << 8));
11084     }
11085 
11086     /**
11087      * Returns the Unicode name of the specified character
11088      * {@code codePoint}, or null if the code point is
11089      * {@link #UNASSIGNED unassigned}.
11090      * <p>
11091      * Note: if the specified character is not assigned a name by
11092      * the <i>UnicodeData</i> file (part of the Unicode Character
11093      * Database maintained by the Unicode Consortium), the returned
11094      * name is the same as the result of expression:
11095      *
11096      * <blockquote>{@code
11097      *     Character.UnicodeBlock.of(codePoint).toString().replace('_', ' ')
11098      *     + " "
11099      *     + Integer.toHexString(codePoint).toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11100      *
11101      * }</blockquote>
11102      *
11103      * @param  codePoint the character (Unicode code point)
11104      *
11105      * @return the Unicode name of the specified character, or null if
11106      *         the code point is unassigned.
11107      *
11108      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified
11109      *            {@code codePoint} is not a valid Unicode
11110      *            code point.
11111      *
11112      * @since 1.7
11113      */
11114     public static String getName(int codePoint) {
11115         if (!isValidCodePoint(codePoint)) {
11116             throw new IllegalArgumentException(
11117                 String.format("Not a valid Unicode code point: 0x%X", codePoint));
11118         }
11119         String name = CharacterName.getInstance().getName(codePoint);
11120         if (name != null)
11121             return name;
11122         if (getType(codePoint) == UNASSIGNED)
11123             return null;
11124         UnicodeBlock block = UnicodeBlock.of(codePoint);
11125         if (block != null)
11126             return block.toString().replace('_', ' ') + " "
11127                    + Integer.toHexString(codePoint).toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11128         // should never come here
11129         return Integer.toHexString(codePoint).toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11130     }
11131 
11132     /**
11133      * Returns the code point value of the Unicode character specified by
11134      * the given Unicode character name.
11135      * <p>
11136      * Note: if a character is not assigned a name by the <i>UnicodeData</i>
11137      * file (part of the Unicode Character Database maintained by the Unicode
11138      * Consortium), its name is defined as the result of expression:
11139      *
11140      * <blockquote>{@code
11141      *     Character.UnicodeBlock.of(codePoint).toString().replace('_', ' ')
11142      *     + " "
11143      *     + Integer.toHexString(codePoint).toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11144      *
11145      * }</blockquote>
11146      * <p>
11147      * The {@code name} matching is case insensitive, with any leading and
11148      * trailing whitespace character removed.
11149      *
11150      * @param  name the Unicode character name
11151      *
11152      * @return the code point value of the character specified by its name.
11153      *
11154      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the specified {@code name}
11155      *         is not a valid Unicode character name.
11156      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code name} is {@code null}
11157      *
11158      * @since 9
11159      */
11160     public static int codePointOf(String name) {
11161         name = name.trim().toUpperCase(Locale.ROOT);
11162         int cp = CharacterName.getInstance().getCodePoint(name);
11163         if (cp != -1)
11164             return cp;
11165         try {
11166             int off = name.lastIndexOf(' ');
11167             if (off != -1) {
11168                 cp = Integer.parseInt(name, off + 1, name.length(), 16);
11169                 if (isValidCodePoint(cp) && name.equals(getName(cp)))
11170                     return cp;
11171             }
11172         } catch (Exception x) {}
11173         throw new IllegalArgumentException("Unrecognized character name :" + name);
11174     }
11175 }
